Baldwin's Speech Advocates Lifting Sanctions Against Italy; Only Way to Avert European War; Advocates Reforming the League of Nations and Promoting Disarmament 39

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin delivered a speech in Lanark yesterday, vigorously defending the British government's attitude of preparing to lift sanctions against Italy, saying that not doing so would only lead to war. He did not advocate taking this action, nor did he know if any country in Europe was prepared to do so. If the League of Nations were always a united association of all countries in the world, then this situation would never occur, because the strength of the member states, except for the aggressor, would be so superior that aggression would not be profitable. The first step in seeking peace through collective security is to increase war preparations, which is a painful irony of the overall situation. If Europe ever rekindles a fire, the spread of this wildfire would be unpredictable. He would not dare to take this risk while holding a little power in the government. The government cannot abandon the hope of bringing countries back to the League of Nations and establishing a practical form of disarmament. Baldwin then described the horrors of a new war for European revival, saying that the government has set a policy to consider how to deal with this issue in Geneva this autumn.

The administrative chairman of the Irish Free State, Eamon de Valera, spoke in Parliament on Friday, supporting British Foreign Secretary Eden's proposal to lift sanctions against Italy and enthusiastically supporting Eden's actions in the Italo-Abyssinian War, saying that the League of Nations' failure to implement an effective plan cannot be blamed on the Foreign Secretary. The people of France have already suffered enough from the European war. Should they not hesitate to consider actions that could lead to war? De Valera also asked those who advocated continuing sanctions whether they were willing to prepare for war. If they were not willing to do so, then they should not criticize those who sought to resolve conflicts and turn swords into plowshares with foresight. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

(London) The Liberal Party held a conference yesterday and passed a resolution stating that it was ashamed and indignant to hear that the government was determined to surrender to the aggressor, betray the League of Nations, and disregard the promises made during the general election. The conference also reaffirmed its loyalty to the League of Nations Covenant, saying that if it were implemented bravely and unyieldingly, it would not fail. Today, various newspapers are discussing what procedures will be used to implement the British government's proposal to lift sanctions against Italy if Geneva accepts it. It is expected that the date of the lifting will be determined by the Sanctions Adjustment Committee and implemented jointly by the governments concerned. Daily news reports state that once a compromise is reached, an order to lift the sanctions plan will not be delayed for long. By mid-July, the sanctions may be completely lifted, and the United Kingdom will announce the lifting by Cabinet order in the same manner as when the sanctions were implemented. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

Countries That Signed the Treaty of Lausanne Hold Meeting Today; Representatives from Nine Countries Attend to Discuss the Issue of Defending the Straits 44

Mond, Switzerland: The countries that signed the Treaty of Lausanne, at the request of Turkey, are convening a meeting to discuss the issue of re-fortifying the Dardanelles and Bosphorus Straits. The meeting is scheduled to open here at 4 pm on the 22nd of this month. Representatives from nine countries, including the United Kingdom, France, Japan, Turkey, Bulgaria, Greece, Romania, Soviet Russia, and Yugoslavia, will attend. The United Kingdom will be represented by the current Minister of Public Works, Lord Stanhope, the former Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs, and France will be represented by former Minister without Portfolio Peng Gu, assisted by Ambassador to Turkey Ponsot. Italy, also a signatory to the Treaty of Lausanne, was also invited to attend, but is expected to be absent in the early stages of the meeting. It is generally hoped that once the sanctions are lifted, the country will be able to send representatives to participate. The scenery here is beautiful and the environment is tranquil. In this early summer, when all kinds of flowers are in full bloom, it feels even more pleasant. It is recalled that before the Lausanne Conference was held in 1923, British Foreign Secretary Lord Curzon, former French Prime Minister Poincaré, and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini met here on November 20, 1922, to exchange opinions, and then signed the Treaty of Lausanne with Turkish representatives in the city of Lausanne the following year. The reason why this meeting is being held in this small town, rather than in the world-famous cities of Lausanne or Geneva, is because the city of Lausanne is opposed by Soviet Russia, and Geneva is opposed by Japan (a Soviet Russian named Vorovsky was previously assassinated in Lausanne, and Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations and does not want to hold meetings in Geneva). The Treaty of Lausanne was signed on July 24, 1923, stipulating that all merchant ships and warships, whether in peacetime or wartime, shall be free to navigate the Dardanelles and Bosphorus Straits, and no defenses may be set up on the shores of the straits or nearby islands. This is tantamount to imposing a military easement on Turkey, which is supervised by an international committee composed of the signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne and the United States. This country has requested the lifting of the restrictions through peaceful and legal means, and it is expected to be satisfied, because the friendly atmosphere between the countries concerned is extremely strong, and they also trust each other, so there are no differences on this issue. (20th Havas Dispatch)

Defendants in Saarland Treason Case Sentenced Separately 45

(Berlin) Fourteen people in the Saarland were accused of plotting subversive activities to the detriment of Germany. French Finance Minister Explains Fiscal Policy; Devaluation of the Franc Has Many Drawbacks; Good Impact on the Market 46

(Paris) Finance Minister Olivar gave an interview to an Echo reporter yesterday to explain the current policy, stating, "There are two ways to solve the financial problem. One is the devaluation of the franc, which is a desperate and immoral solution. The only people who benefit from the drawbacks are speculators. The second is that France's viability is inherently rich and sound, and it must be stimulated. This is an optimistic solution. We have already made a choice between the two, and only confidence and health remain. The economic panic encountered by the United States was even worse than that of our country. The people of that country are now emerging from their plight, and they have been able to understand the way to achieve this. Why should the people of France be ignorant and pessimistic? You can ignore the alarmist rhetoric. On the contrary, you should continue to trust France and trust French doctors. It is not a good thing that these doctors do not advocate bloodletting or amputation, but use other methods to treat chronic diseases," and so on. (21st Havas Dispatch)

(London) The rescue measures for the franc announced by French Finance Minister Oreval in the House of Commons have had a good impact. The prices of various gold coins rose this morning, but the financial community is reluctant to comment hastily because several key points are not yet clear. If the Blum government's plan had not failed, reducing the currency value would never have been tried lightly. Therefore, short sellers must engage in covering, and the franc can naturally turn around. A London banker told a Reuters reporter that the French Finance Minister is determined to fight to the end and will not reduce the currency value, because if he yields, the expectations of the French Socialist Party will be completely wiped out, and it may not be possible to recover in twenty years. As to whether the plan put forward by the French Finance Minister can remedy the financial panic he described, there are still many people who doubt it. A glimpse of the comment of the Times can be seen. The newspaper said that the case of the French Finance Minister making people report the money stored abroad may not reduce but will increase the outflow of funds, because hoarders are deeply worried that the government will even be engaged in finding out where the funds are before trying to balance the budget and put the currency on a more solid basis, so as to implement a method of requisition. (20th Reuters Dispatch)

France; Demonstrations by the Croix-de-Feu; Disturbances Continue in Various Places 47

(Paris) Since the government ordered the dissolution of various paramilitary groups, many disturbances have occurred in the capital and other provinces. By the afternoon, 300 men and women had gathered at the Star Square, shouting "Long live Colonel de la Rocque, long live the Croix-de-Feu!" (Note: de la Rocque is the leader of the Croix-de-Feu.) The leader of the group, fearing an incident, advised them to disperse, but to no effect. The police arrested several people. The Croix-de-Feu headquarters in Saint-Étienne has been closed. The members then formed a team to go to the World War Memorial for a demonstration and sang the national anthem. On the way, they clashed with members of the Popular Front, injuring several people. In Saint-Étienne, newsboys from the royalist Action Française and the communist Avant-Garde fought each other, injuring several people. The police restored order. In Amiens, members of the Patriotic Youth League marched out with the blue, white, and red flags (the French national flag) and armbands. Striking workers saw them and immediately stepped forward to seize them, resulting in disturbances. The police stopped them. (21st Havas Dispatch)

Belgium; Labor Strike Has Taken a Turn; Compromise Reached Between Labor and Management in the Mining Industry 48

Brussels: According to an announcement by the Ministry of the Interior yesterday, the strike situation in Belgium has now taken a turn. There was only a small conflict in Ghent. The striking workers threatened to come here in teams. The authorities have sent troops to block the roads, but the workers do not seem likely to take this action. Labor and management in the mining industry reached a compromise yesterday on the following three points: The minimum daily wage is 32 francs; Recognition of the labor union; Vacation wages will be paid. Most other industries have accepted the recommendations of the arbitration committee. The employer's request for a 40-hour work week for workers is now awaiting government decision. The Cabinet meeting today will discuss this matter. A Socialist senator was conscripted by the gendarmerie in the mining area to repair the roads destroyed by the striking workers. The man has not yet obtained a parliamentary immunity certificate. Because the employer has allowed a daily wage increase of 12 francs, the dockworkers in Antwerp agreed yesterday to resume work on Sunday. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

Brussels: Dockworkers in the port of Antwerp have signed an agreement with their employers. There have been several cases of workers destroying machinery in the city of Ghent. Several workers have been arrested. (21st Havas Dispatch)

Brussels: The labor strike situation in Belgium remains tense. The government has recently decided to take special emergency measures, such as mobilizing troops to strengthen the police force. It is said that miners in Borinage and Charleroi are planning to march in teams to the capital. The government has mobilized troops to guard the main roads between the capital and Charleroi to prevent this. Troops are also stationed on the roads in the southern province of Brabant that lead directly to the capital. Barbed wire has been set up near the city of Halle to guard it. Strikers in various places are flying red flags everywhere in the streets to persuade workers to join the strike movement. So far, although some industries have reached agreements between labor and management, only the dockworkers in the port of Antwerp have resumed work. (20th Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) Twenty-six thousand employees of various department stores, who had been on strike for eighteen days, reached an agreement yesterday through the mediation of Interior Minister Salengro. (Tokyo) The Hirota Cabinet, aiming for a complete renewal of national affairs, will hold a cabinet meeting on the 3rd of next month to discuss important national policies. Prior to this cabinet meeting, the three chief secretaries of the cabinet, Fujinuma, Ketsuda, and Yoshida, will be responsible for coordinating and adjusting among the various ministries in order to smoothly determine national policies. This will provide Prime Minister Hirota with the basis for making final decisions on national policies. Therefore, they will first review the various national policies proposed by each ministry and draft original proposals. The important national policies that are likely to be implemented from the next fiscal year include the national defense policies of the army and navy, the iron and fuel national policies of the Ministry of Commerce and Industry, and the electricity control and aviation national policies of the Ministry of Communications. The decisions also include the industrialization of rural villages, reform of the education system, and the national health and welfare system. (Domei dispatch, 21st)

(Tokyo) The new policies of the Hirota Cabinet, which will be presented to the world, will be discussed in detail at the two cabinet meetings on July 3rd and 10th. Each cabinet member will bring concrete items under the jurisdiction of their respective ministries. After careful deliberation and consultation at the cabinet meetings, they will strive to decide on the national policies that must be implemented by August 10th. The major national policies proposed by each cabinet member are currently expected to be roughly as follows:

Policies to actively assist in the construction of Chinese railways and other economic cooperation with China, proposal to establish a new trade control agency, proposal to establish an independent health administration agency, plan to implement rural social policies, plan to reorganize central and local finances, plan to increase taxes, plan to establish additional monopoly systems, plan to expand troop strength in Manchuria, plan to increase inland divisions and other army national defense plans, navy's five-year national defense replenishment plan, proposal to establish a Ministry of Aviation or Bureau of Aviation, plan to implement an eight-year compulsory education system, plan to implement an agricultural insurance system, iron and steel national policy plan, plan to subsidize the coal liquefaction industry, electricity control plan, proposal to establish a minister without portfolio. When the Prime Minister decides on these important national policy items, he will not hesitate to adopt as many as possible that are truly national policies, important, and desired by all parties, as long as they are financially feasible. Therefore, which policies will be adopted as the current cabinet's policies is highly noteworthy. (Domei dispatch, 21st)

Scientists from Various Countries Successfully Observe Solar Eclipse, Results to be Published Within Six Months 72

(Moscow) Dr. Montréal, the leader of the American observation team, telegraphed Moscow, saying, "The observation was successful. Congratulations to all Soviet astronomers and thank the Soviet government for its assistance. The results of the work will be published within at least six months."

The weather at Shala Station was good. Two Soviet teams, one Italian team, and one Czech team all successfully completed their planned projects. Akbulak reported that a special train came here from Orenburg to observe the solar eclipse. The scientists looked up at the clouds with great anxiety, and upon learning that the clouds would not hinder the observation, they also saw a large swarm of locusts flying across the sky, but they were dispersed by airplanes, and the observation was completely successful.

Professor Carroll, the leader of the British observation team in Omsk, said, "I have traveled to various countries to observe solar eclipses four times, but all have failed. Only here have I succeeded completely. I thank the local authorities and my Soviet colleagues for their assistance. Without this, this success would not have been possible. (TASS dispatch, 21st)

(Moscow) During the solar eclipse on June 19th, a stratospheric balloon was launched to a height of 9,200 meters in Omsk. The balloon remained airborne for five hours. Moscow also launched a balloon to take pictures of the solar eclipse. In Krasnodar, scientists observed from an airplane at a height of 5,300 meters, where the temperature was minus 25 degrees Celsius. Stratospheric balloons were also used to observe the solar eclipse in that area. (TASS dispatch, 21st)

Korma: Dr. Shinjō, director of the Shanghai Natural Science Institute, who was in charge of the department of geo-magnetic changes at the solar eclipse observation in Korma, achieved great success. He spoke about the results of the observation that day as follows:

"This solar eclipse observation relied entirely on clear skies, so there was a great harvest. At this crucial moment, the vertical line of the magnetic meter was suddenly cut off, and the battery suddenly broke. It was a failure, but after emergency measures were taken, it was restored, and all the observations were completely completed. The results of this observation will be temporarily taken back to the research room, and it will be difficult to know the exact results without a month. If the observations in other places fail, then the observation in Korma can be said to be the best in the world, and it will cause a great shock in the scientific community." (Domei News Agency dispatch, 21st)

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

General Situation of China's National Wealth and International Relations (II) 75

— Zhang Qiyun

In recent years, food has consistently ranked first among China's imported goods. Taking 1935 as an example, the total value of imported rice, wheat, flour, and other grains amounted to 136 million yuan, roughly equivalent to two-fifths of the trade deficit (243.1 million yuan). In recent years, the average trade deficit in rice and wheat accounts for about 4% of the national average production (calculated with wheat and flour, where every 100 catties of wheat can be made into 70 catties of flour). It is generally common for industrial countries to be unable to be self-sufficient in food. However, China's industry is underdeveloped, the number of farmers is far greater in comparison, and even the people's food supply relies on foreign countries, with annual outflows exceeding 100 million yuan. If something happens in East Asia and overseas sources are cut off, a food panic is highly concerning. There are, of course, many ways to solve the food problem, such as reclaiming wasteland, improving farming methods, banning opium cultivation, preventing famines, improving marketing organizations, adjusting surpluses and deficits among provinces, restoring accumulated grain storage, maintaining balanced grain prices, and also appropriately determining import tariffs to protect domestic agricultural products, so that the phenomenon of foreign rice encroaching on the market and low grain prices hurting farmers can be eliminated in the future. It is a well-known fact that one of the reasons for Germany's defeat in the European War was the shortage of food. Guaranteeing the food supply for the people and the army is the most crucial task.

China's annual cotton production is 13 million dan (average from 1933 to 1935), with the Yangtze and Yellow River basins each accounting for half. China's cotton production often falls short of meeting domestic consumption needs. In 1934, when there was a good domestic cotton harvest, the total value of imports was 40 million yuan, while in 1934 it was 90 million yuan. Most imported cotton comes from India and the United States. Indian cotton wins in quantity, while American cotton wins in quality. The ordinary quality of Chinese cotton is not good, with very short fibers, so ways to improve it must be found. Silk, tea, and soybeans have always been China's major exports. Soybean exports from the eastern provinces have historically been relied upon to offset the majority of the food trade deficit, but this is no longer the case. Raw silk is a sideline for farm families in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Guangdong provinces and is highly valued. In 1935, the total silkworm cocoon production was 1.4 million dan, and the total raw silk production was 95,000 dan, of which Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces accounted for slightly less than two-thirds, and Guangdong accounted for slightly less than one-quarter. Raw silk exports and domestic consumption each account for about half. China's tea production is over 5 million dan, with annual exports of around 1 million dan, worth about 20 million yuan. In addition, there is a shortage of economic crops such as sugar cane and tobacco raw materials. Over the years, foreign sugar and tobacco have been important import items. Timber is also a major import, with recent import amounts exceeding 30 million yuan, mostly for construction purposes, and a significant number of railroad ties. Moreover, it increases annually. Timber is a commodity with very low transport capacity, due to its bulk and weight, its price is extremely low, so to develop mountains and forests, one must start by improving transportation and saving on labor costs. Among forestry by-products, tung oil and tussah silk are the most valuable. In 1936, tung oil exports reached a staggering 40 million yuan, ranking second among export goods, which was unprecedented. Tussah silk is used not only for weaving silk but also as a material for aircraft wings, while tung oil is used for aircraft coatings, so demand has increased greatly in recent years. China produces about 20,000 dan of tussah silk, centered in Liaoning, with recent exports reaching 20 million yuan. Rubber is a tropical product and has a wide range of uses in modern industry. Hainan Island is the only place in China where rubber can be grown. China's animal husbandry can be divided into two major regions: the central region and the three northeastern provinces are agricultural regions, while the northwest border region is a nomadic region, with the Greater Khingan Range and the Yin Mountains as their natural boundaries. In the former, animal husbandry is a sideline for farmers, while in the latter, animal husbandry is the only means of livelihood. The northwest provinces produce 600,000 dan of wool and 100,000 dan of camel hair annually, mostly exported from Tianjin. According to 1935 statistics, the export value of wool, camel hair, hides, and carpets totaled 40 million yuan. Hides are mostly obtained through hunting, while carpets are mostly hand-woven products. There is still a lack of accurate statistics on the total number of horses in China. Recently, equine administration has been neglected, and it is feared that strong warhorses are no longer readily available. Improving horses is crucial for military purposes. Meat is scarce in rural areas, so fish are heavily relied upon to supplement the deficiency. The state of China's fishing industry has not been thoroughly investigated. In 1935, imports of fish and seafood were nearly 20 million yuan, which shows the decline of the fishing industry. The development of the fishing industry is linked to shipping and the navy. Salt tax is a major source of revenue for China. The total salt production in the country is over 55 million dan, of which sea salt accounts for 20%. China's salt production is more than self-sufficient, with annual exports of 6 million dan to Japan and Korea.

Among China's minerals, coal is the most important. According to estimates by the Geological Survey, the nation's coal reserves are 246 billion tons, ranking third in the world, behind the United States and Canada. However, calculated per capita, each person only gets 500 tons, which is less than the United States' 10,000 tons per person, Britain's 4,000 tons, and Germany's 1,500 tons, only exceeding Japan's 100 tons per person. The coal reserves in each province are very unevenly distributed, with Shanxi Province accounting for 52% of the national total, and Shaanxi Province accounting for 29%. The two together account for 81%, which is more than four-fifths. It is said that if Shanxi's coal mines can be developed, it would be like Britain in Western Europe and Pennsylvania in the United States. China's important coalfields are all in North China, and it is very concerning that the coal industry would be devastated in the event of war. In 1933, China's total coal production was over 28 million tons, ranking eighth in the world, even ahead of Japan. In that year, the four northeastern provinces produced over 9 million tons of coal, accounting for one-third. China's iron ore is quite scarce, with national reserves of 1.02 billion tons, averaging only 2.5 tons per person. Liaoning Province alone accounts for 77% of the national iron ore reserves, and Chahar accounts for 9%. Liaoning is to iron as Shanxi and Shaanxi are to coal; the Bohai Sea and the Yellow River are the lifeline of China's mineral resources. Liaoning's iron ore is second only to India in East Asia and has now become an overseas base for Japan's steel industry. Japan's iron production capacity is 1.5 million tons per year, and steel production has reached 2.1 million tons, so Japan not only needs ore from abroad but also needs to absorb raw iron from India and Liaoning as raw materials. According to 1933 statistics, the iron ore production in Anshan, Benxi, and other iron mines in Liaoning was 500,000 tons, but in reality, we no longer own it. The iron industry in the interior is extremely depressed, producing only tens of thousands of tons per year. The iron ore in Hubei and Anhui provinces in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River is all exported to Japan, which is no different from working for others. The annual iron production using indigenous methods throughout the country is also only 100,000 tons, mostly consumed in local iron foundries. In terms of the current national demand for steel, it reaches 600,000 tons per year, mostly relying on imports from Britain and Japan. In 1934 and 1935, the average import of steel was 80 million yuan, accounting for 8% of the total national imports. China's oil reserves are estimated to be 3.6 billion barrels (40 gallons per barrel), of which oil shale in Fushun contains 1.9 billion barrels, accounting for 53% of the total national reserves. Fushun's oil shale is the richest in East Asia, almost one-third of the United States or Russia, and one-twentieth of the world's total, so its importance is evident. China's oil production is extremely scarce, but Fushun stands out exceptionally, with a production of 80,000 tons in 1933, and it is estimated that it can produce 300,000 tons per year. Among China's inland oilfields, Shaanxi is the most promising, with both natural oil and oil shale, and oil wells have been explored, with good results, but the output is still negligible, so China must rely on foreign oil, at least for the time being. In 1933, the import of oil, including kerosene, diesel, and gasoline, totaled 75 million yuan, of which kerosene accounted for half, and diesel and gasoline each accounted for a quarter. China's gold and silver production is very small, around 100,000 taels each. There is a surplus of tin ore but a shortage of copper ore. The national tin production is 9,000 tons per year, with 90% coming from Yunnan, a single old tin mine. The annual consumption of copper is 6,000 tons, but the production is only about one-tenth. Copper is an electrical material and is indirectly related to military affairs. China's antimony and tungsten mines are particularly abundant. Hunan's antimony and Jiangxi's tungsten can both be the best in the world. Both are related to the manufacture of munitions, so they have attracted worldwide attention. The world's antimony production is 16,000 tons, and China produces two-fourths. The world's tungsten production is 14,000 tons, and China produces a strong two-fifths. These two minerals have no market in China and are almost entirely exported, subject to foreign merchants manipulating prices. If we could set up our own refineries and study their uses, wouldn't these rare metals be rare commodities to hold? The use of aluminum is growing daily, and the raw materials for airplanes require a lot. Aluminum can be extracted from alunite, and Pingyang, Zhejiang, has as much as 2 billion tons of alunite. If the extraction test is successful, it is hoped that it will become one of the countries with the most aluminum production in the world.

China's modern industry is represented by the cotton textile industry. According to 1934 statistics, there were a total of 133 yarn factories in the country, with a total of 5.2 million spindles, of which Chinese merchants owned 56%, Japanese merchants owned 40%, and British merchants owned 4%. Among the factories, there are 43,000 power looms, of which Chinese merchants own 48%, Japanese merchants own 45%, and British merchants own 7%. The number of spindles per thousand people in China is still the lowest among the major cotton textile countries in the world. Britain is the hegemon of this industry, with 1,200 spindles per thousand people. Japan also has 100 spindles per thousand people, while China only has 12 spindles per thousand people. If only Chinese yarn factories are counted, there are still less than 7 spindles per thousand people. After the Russo-Japanese War, Japan was able to meet domestic needs and developed overseas markets. Japan's exports of cotton textiles to China accounted for half. China's cotton textile industry is constantly threatened, namely, the competition from foreign yarn factories inside and outside China and the dumping of foreign imported cotton goods. As a result, some Chinese spinning factories that are operating at a loss are gradually being acquired by Japanese companies. In 1935, the import of cotton, cotton yarn, and cotton cloth reached 65 million yuan (of which cotton yarn and cotton cloth accounted for 23 million yuan), accounting for one-ninth of the trade deficit in the same year. In terms of the geographical distribution of China's cotton textile industry, Shanghai accounts for more than half. Combined with Wuxi and Nantong, Jiangsu Province accounts for two-thirds of the country, its important status like Lancashire in Britain and Osaka in Japan. Raw silk is the largest export for both China and Japan, and the United States is the largest market for both. After the war, Japanese cotton cloth sales spread to India and Southeast Asia, and in recent years, they have expanded to Africa and the Near East, replacing raw silk as the top export. The market price of raw silk is unlikely to rise due to the pressure from rayon. China's silk industry has been very depressed in recent years, and its first export position has long been replaced by soybeans. Last year, it was below tung oil and ranked second. In 1930, there were more than 180 silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, with more than 55,000 machines. Due to the low price of silk in Europe and the United States, three-fifths of them were suspended or closed down. One reason for the failure of the silk industry is the dumping of cheap Japanese silk, and the other is the rise of rayon. In 1935, China's raw silk exports were 35 million yuan, accounting for 2% of the total exports. In the same year, rayon imports were 7 million yuan, and much of it was used to interweave with natural silk and cotton yarn. China's wool textile industry is very underdeveloped. The output of domestic woolen mills is only 1 million yuan. In 1935, the import of woolen fabrics and wool yarn totaled 13 million yuan. At present, the demand for woolen products is increasing, and it is necessary to improve wool and increase textile production. Although the price of raw silk is higher than that of wool, because it is a domestic product, there is room for research in the uniforms of the military and political circles. The total value of China's machine paper-making industry is nearly 10 million yuan. During its heyday, the annual value of handmade paper was 50 million yuan, but recently it has been less than 20 million yuan. In total, domestic paper production is less than 30 million yuan, but China's annual consumption of paper is about 70 million yuan, with an annual deficit of 40 million yuan, relying on imports. European paper imports account for two-fifths, and Japanese imports account for one-third. The nature of newspapers is different from other enterprises. The importance of the news industry is even greater during wartime than in peacetime. The establishment of newspaper mills should not be regarded as a slow plan. China's cement consumption is 6 million barrels per year, and the production of domestic cement plants is 4 million barrels. The deficit is imported from abroad, and the value of imported cement is 2 million yuan per year. Porcelain is a traditional industry in China, with a total national output of 20 million yuan. Japan's total output of ceramics is 80 million yen, and China is far behind. In recent years, the import and export value of Chinese ceramics has often been a deficit.

China's industrial base has not yet been established. Ordinary industries such as cotton weaving and cement industries are not yet developed, and basic industries have very few achievements. The so-called basic industries are those whose products cannot be directly supplied to consumers but are used as tools for general industries, such as the machinery industry. Machinery is mostly related to the steel industry, so it is called heavy industry. The importance of basic industries is often far greater than their own monetary value, such as the products of the chemical industry. These industries are mostly large-scale and cannot be undertaken by private enterprises. Moreover, because they are closely related to national interests and people's welfare, they should be operated by the state. The current situation of the decline of China's steel industry has been mentioned above. As for machinery factories, most of them lack capital and are small in scale. In 1935, the import value of machinery (including textile machinery, electrical machinery, and other tools) was 15.5 million yuan, which indicates that China's modern industry is gradually developing, but it is also a great deficit in the national economy. The Ministry of Industry is planning to establish a China Machinery Manufacturing Factory, which is a major task at present. According to the Statistics of the Construction Committee in 1934, there were more than 460 power plants in the country, with a power generation capacity of 480,000 kilowatts (that is, 640,000 horsepower, excluding the three northeastern provinces). Although only 11 of them are operated by foreigners, their power generation capacity accounts for half, such as the Shanghai Electric Power Company, which accounts for 200,000 horsepower, and most of the power for Shanghai factories is supplied by this. China's power plants all use coal as fuel and are called thermal power plants. The hydropower business is still under exploration. According to the plan of the Construction Committee, the first hydropower plant will be set up at the Three Gorges of the Yangtze River in Yichang, with a capacity of 300,000 kilowatts (that is, 400,000 horsepower), and the construction cost is estimated to be 400 million yuan. Hydropower plants are closely related to the chemical industry, and there are very few chemical industries in China, far from enough. In recent years, the products of the chemical industry such as rayon, artificial fertilizers, and dyes have been imported in large quantities, and the manufacture of explosives and toxic gases is also related to the chemical industry. They make a great contribution to national defense. Shipbuilding is also one of the basic industries. It is said that ships are the lifeline of Britain's national wealth, and Japan's various mechanical industries are also related to shipbuilding. Because shipbuilding is developed, the shipping industry is prosperous, and because maritime transportation is developed, the navy is also strong. China's warships total 27,500 tons, with 2/5 self-made, 1/4 made by Germany and Japan and 1/7 from Britain. The Jiangnan Shipyard made 3/5 of the self-made warships, and the Mawei Shipyard made just over 1/4. Japanese shipyards can also manufacture airplanes, so the Japanese Air Force has a strong potential force. As for the automobiles and processed tank vehicles used by the army, the technology of Japanese factories is also improving with each passing year. According to the 1934 statistics, there were 50,000 cars in China. According to Mr. Yao Xiguang's statistics (see the English China Yearbook in 1935), there were 433 military aircraft and 24 naval aircraft. Almost all cars and airplanes are foreign products, which is a pity from the perspective of national defense. All far-sighted governments spare no effort to encourage basic industries, without saying anything superfluous.

Modern transportation is what China lacks most at present. According to 1933 statistics, the total length of railways in the country was only 18,000 kilometers, of which the length of state-owned railways was more than 12,000 kilometers, accounting for more than two-thirds of the total railway length in the country, the length of private railways was 2,400 kilometers, and the length of railways contracted by foreigners was more than 3,300 kilometers, accounting for 30% of the total railway length in the country. In 1935, the total length of newly built railway lines such as Yuehan, Longhai, Zhegan, and Tongpu was 1,700 kilometers, which is less than 20,000 kilometers in total, which is far from the 400,000 kilometers of railways in the United States. In 1934, the Japanese state-owned railway was 16,000 kilometers, plus the private railway was about 8,000 kilometers, a total of more than 24,000 kilometers, with an average of one kilometer of railway per 4,000 people, while in China, there is only one kilometer of railway per 20,000 people. Most of the major railway lines in China are north of the Yangtze River, and the three northeastern provinces account for the most, accounting for 2/5 of the total railway investment in the country, which we no longer own. The total tonnage of China's merchant ships is only 400,000 tons, which is only one-tenth of Japan's. Japan's merchant ships total more than 4.3 million tons (1934 statistics), making it the world's third largest shipping country, with annual freight of 200 million yuan (Japanese currency) contributed to the motherland from overseas goods. In China, there is a current lack of giant seagoing ships, and foreign trade relies entirely on other people's ships. Even in coastal trade, most of it relies on foreign merchant ships. (To be continued)

Private Goods Piled Up at Jinan Station 76

The Railway Anti-Smuggling Department Has No Way to Stop It

Jinan Correspondence: In recent days, the smuggling of goods from Tianjin to Jinan has been increasing. Previously, they were transported by train No. 309 of the Pingpu Line, which arrived in Jinan at about 9:00 am. Now, train No. 21 of the Jinpu Line, which arrives in Jinan at about 8:00 pm, also carries a large number of smuggled goods, which are surging more and more. There is still no way to stop it. This morning (the 19th), train No. 305 was loaded with smuggled goods, and the number was even greater, with 787 pieces of rayon, 70 pieces of sugar, 12 pieces of cloth ends, 7 pieces of cigarette paper, and 12 pieces of materials, totaling 888 pieces. There were also sixteen or seventeen packages wrapped in paper, shaped like biscuit boxes, which were very heavy, but it is not known what they were. Except for the first and second-class sleeping cars and the dining car, there were no smuggled goods. The four third-class cars and one second-class scattered-seat car were all fully loaded with bags and mat bags. Except for a few smugglers, there was not a single passenger on the train. The smuggled goods were unloaded on the platform, forming a small mountain. It took an hour to move them. The bicycle left. To prevent it, Li Tonghua, deputy director of the Railway Anti-Smuggling Department, is scheduled to take train No. 202 of the Pinghu Line to Tianjin at 8:00 pm tonight to report to An Sier, director of the General Department, and then go to Beijing to report to the Ministry of Finance on the recent situation of smuggling in North China and ask for fundamental prevention measures. The smugglers, because the smuggled goods could not be transported to the south, went to the station to contact Wang Yongzeng, the station master, offering a bribe of 2 yuan per package to allow them to be transported to the south. Wang sternly refused and reported the situation of temptation to his superiors. The smugglers had no choice but to become dissatisfied with Wang.

Shandong Province Unifies Tax Collection 77

Tax Collection Offices Established in Various Counties, Various Tax Bureaus Abolished

Jinan Correspondence: Wang Xiangrong, Director of the Department of Finance, in order to unify the tax collection in various counties, according to the resolution of the previous National Financial Conference, has uniformly established tax collection offices in various counties throughout the province. The county government no longer concurrently handles this work. After the establishment of the tax collection offices, the various tax bureaus that have been established in various counties are abolished. Various county treasuries are also established uniformly in various counties as collection and remittance agencies. This measure is an unprecedented major reform in the province's finances. The principles have been submitted to the provincial government's political affairs meeting and approved. In order to facilitate the implementation, the Department of Finance recently convened administrative commissioners from various districts to Jinan to study and has made a complete decision. Therefore, the Department is drafting the temporary regulations and budgets for the tax collection offices and county treasuries in various counties, which will be submitted to the provincial government's political affairs meeting today (the 19th) for discussion and resolution, and will be promulgated for implementation immediately. It is stipulated that the counties within the commissioner districts must establish tax collection offices and county treasuries by the 25th year of the Republic (according to the regulations, various counties merge the first and third sections to establish county treasuries. Various counties within the commissioner districts have already merged the second and third sections). The remaining counties are also required to establish tax collection offices uniformly from the 25th year of the Republic and report their establishment in July of this year, merge the second and third sections, and establish county treasuries, which must also be realized by September of this year. Detailed measures for the tax collection offices: Except for Zouping and Heze counties, the 103 counties in the province are divided into 11 districts, including Jinan, Jining, Zhoucun, Weixian, Qingdao, Linqing, Yantai, Linyi, Bochuan, Tengxian, Zaozhuang, etc. The gold and silver collected by the tax collection offices in various counties are kept in the treasuries and remitted to the provincial treasury through nearby Minsheng Bank, Ping City Official Money Bureau, China Transportation Bank, etc. The scope of collection by the tax collection offices has also been stipulated, including land tax, surtax, livestock, slaughter, oil, tooth, and various business taxes, the ordinary business tax handled on behalf of the government, tobacco and alcohol license tax, and all local donations and taxes in various counties, etc., are the responsibility of the tax collection offices, which must have a guarantee of 10,000 yuan. The county treasuries must also have a guarantee of 10,000 yuan. According to statistics, the annual expenses of the tax collection offices in 103 counties total 574,117 yuan.

The Boundary Between Jiangsu and Anhui Provinces Is Clearly Demarcated

The authorities of the two provinces also have difficulty dealing with it. Yesterday, Hou Hongkai, the construction commissioner of Wu County, the representative of Gao, and Liu Yigong, the county chief of Dangtu, directly surveyed the boundary. Specialists from the Ministry of Interior also participated. From now on, it will be able to be clearly demarcated and eliminate disputes forever. (June 10)

Hubei Province: Anti-Drug Achievements 79

Total Confiscation Exceeds Tens of Thousands of Smokers

Hankou Communication: Hubei Province has long been an area rife with opium and drugs. Western and Northern Hubei were also opium poppy production areas. Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek issued strict orders to prohibit them, opium poppies have disappeared, and the smuggling, sale, and consumption of opium have also decreased significantly. Now that the general inspection has been completed, the achievements are quite impressive. According to statistics from the main operating agency, in 70 counties across the province:

* 6,678 opium dens were sealed up.

* 692 opium-related criminal cases were cracked, including 24 smuggling cases and 668 cases of illegal sale and consumption.

* 221 drug-related criminal cases were cracked, with 4 serious offenders executed by firing squad, 2 sentenced to life imprisonment, 120 sentenced to imprisonment for up to six years, and 13 sentenced to imprisonment for up to three years.

* 124 drug rehabilitation hospitals and centers were established, including 105 opium rehabilitation hospitals and 19 drug rehabilitation centers.

* 20,062 opium smokers were forcibly rehabilitated, and 41,919 people quit opium voluntarily.

* A total of 240,118 opium smokers were registered. Among them, over 160,000 were registered by the end of the month, and over 170,000 were registered during the supplementary registration period ending June 15th.

* A total of 115,057 "gong suo" (a unit of weight) of drugs and opium materials were burned, including six categories: morphine, heroin, red pills, opium dross, compound substances, and poppy seeds. (20th)

Suzhou: Land Court Establishes Notary Office 83

Wuxian County Method, In order to implement the notarization system, a report was submitted to the legal administration and approved. It was decided to start operating from July 1st and establish a notary office in the court. From then on, the people's legal actions or other facts regarding private rights may request the judge of the notary office to issue a notarized document, or to certify a private document, and the power of official notarization can be obtained. There are four benefits to the notarization system: Notarized documents or certified private documents are used by the court as the basis for judgment, far beyond the effectiveness of private documents and statement filings. Notarized documents can be used as the basis for compulsory enforcement, saving the loss of seeking litigation. The original notarized document and the copy of the certified private document are permanently preserved by the court, without fear of loss or destruction. The certificate can protect the legal privacy of the parties. This notarization system is still a pioneering effort in Jiangsu Province. After this implementation, many disputes can be avoided.

After actively proceeding with the construction, most of it has been completed and can be put into use to facilitate the transportation of commercial goods.

Discussion on the Implementation Plan for National Economic Construction (Part 2) 96

— Zhu Ping

4. Principles of National Economic Construction

(1) The factors of production are "human power," "land power," and "capital power." The development of production activities must adopt a "human power" and "land power" combination and give it the power to make reasonable placements and applications so that it becomes a systematic and consciously planned activity. Therefore, the allocation of production factors is not something that can be accomplished overnight. National economic development is not something that can be done in a short period. Therefore, the only way to proceed is to make practical adjustments and combinations to the existing economic and production units, so that they become an organized body, and then they can be purposefully and systematically unified.

(2) The construction of national economy should take the entire nation as the goal. Under the current national situation, it is especially important to carefully examine the geographical situation of transportation in various places. All the establishment of basic industries and the construction of major projects must be selected in safe zones with emphasis on defense.

(3) The county should be regarded as the basic regional unit of the national economic organization. All production, exchange, consumption, and transportation within the county should be the economic scope. Efforts should be made to make the organizational structure and commercial activities of the county vigorous and beneficial to the economic movement of the county, while also being suitable for individual survival.

(4) Local defense organizations and educational undertakings should be integrated with economic construction, so that they can mutually assist and promote each other under the overall goal.

(5) "Human power" is the most important element of production. To build a national economy, all social "human power" should be assigned in a planned manner. All adult men and women (assumed to be 18 to 45 years old) have the obligation to serve and work, and the period of service should be stipulated according to the actual needs of various places.

(6) The number of adult men and women in each county and the nature of their abilities—such as being suitable for working, farming, serving in the military, or serving as doctors, nurses, or teachers—should be thoroughly investigated and registered separately for mobilization at any time.

(7) In order to facilitate the mobilization and control of "human power," the registered "human power" should be given strict organization and appropriate training. In addition to cultivating their production skills and the spirit of group work, the training of "human power" must also teach them self-defense capabilities, so that they can protect the safety of their economic construction within the possible range with self-defense forces.

(8) Land is a necessary tool for production. Each county should measure and estimate the area of various types of land within its territory, and control its utilization and adjust its ownership relationships.

(9) Actively carry out irrigation, dredging, filling, and other water conservancy projects to increase arable land area.

(10) Landless farmers should be provided with land as much as possible, so as to make full use of "human power" and increase "land power."

(11) Establish model farms in various places as appropriate, apply appropriate scientific methods and machinery to improve productivity and increase production.

(12) Improve the production capacity of model farms and encourage farmers to automatically adopt new farming techniques or organize cooperatives to improve agricultural management and increase agricultural production. The government must give special treatment to cooperatives (such as the use of public machinery, technical guidance, transportation convenience, economic assistance, and the establishment of cultural defense facilities) to promote farmers' engagement in collective production.

(13) Sidelines are the tail end for farmers to absorb surplus labor, and their impact on farmers' income is very large. The government must provide practical guidance according to the distribution of sidelines in various places, improve their products, and increase their production.

(14) Establish a sound rural credit organization, adjust rural finance, and support the development of emerging cooperative fields and general agriculture.

(15) All large-scale and basic industries should be operated or supervised by the government, and investment by domestic and foreign capital should be encouraged with appropriate conditions or lease operation methods.

(16) The government should encourage and improve various handicrafts with special effectiveness according to the operating conditions of each handicraft, in order to make up for the current shortage of mechanical production.

(17) According to the government's financial resources and needs, gradually distribute the power grid to various places to supply light, heat, electricity, and other power required for residence, manufacturing, and transportation.

(18) The construction of light industrial plants must meet the following principles:

In areas near the place where raw materials are produced, manufacturing of various related industrial products should be concentrated as much as possible, so that production costs can be reduced and product standards can be unified.

Small-scale factories should be widely established in rural central areas within the possible scope to facilitate farmers' participation in manufacturing work, so that the countryside will not be deserted due to population reduction, and cities will not be crowded due to too many factories, creating a poor social environment. The distribution of households can also be balanced, and resources in various places can be universally developed, so that even in the event of violent destruction, only a part will be affected.

(19) Under the principle of guaranteeing facility safety and safeguarding labor welfare, efforts should be made to adjust labor-management relations and work together to seek the development of the entire national economy.

(20) The exchange of commodities should be given appropriate control, so as to shorten the distance between producers and consumers, and between raw material suppliers and manufacturers.

(21) The import and export of commodities in each locality must be organized by the local commercial associations to jointly organize import and export trade hubs. All import and export of commodities must be handled through the general hub. Any individual actions will be sanctioned by the same industry.

(22) The types, quantities, and sources of consumer goods in various places, as well as the types, quantities, and marketing areas of local products, should be thoroughly investigated and statistically analyzed to gradually rationalize the exchange of commodities. Non-essential consumer goods that are not manufactured in this country should be restricted as much as possible.

(23) Commodity prices should be rationally controlled to protect the appropriate level of profit for producers and balance the profits of sellers.

(24) Financial institutions in various places should be concentrated under the entire economic construction plan to fully utilize their functions.

(25) The construction of transportation should be made suitable for the needs of economic construction and national defense, and the central government and provincial and county governments should design and implement it within their professional scope.

(26) The implementation of economic construction must rely on a large number of specialized talents or personnel with appropriate education to participate. At the beginning, existing personnel serving in central and local party and government agencies can be transferred to various places according to their abilities and assigned to various appropriate jobs.

(27) The policies concerning education at all levels of schools must be as closely aligned as possible with the needs of economic construction. At the same time, the activities of various cultural organizations should concentrate their efforts on conducting widespread publicity and mobilization for economic construction.

Ge Jiachen of the Woolen Cloth Industry Discusses Three Principles to Prevent Smuggling 105

The Shanghai Woolen Cloth Industry Association, due to the rampant smuggling of goods, which has greatly affected the industry, sent Ge Jiachen to the Customs to visit the Chief Inspector of Customs, Moyler, to request consideration for the legitimate interests of traders and to assist in suppressing smuggling. Moyler expressed acceptance and said that the methods needed to be discussed at length. A reporter from Xin Sheng She interviewed Ge yesterday. According to him, the smuggled goods from a certain country to Shanghai only pay 7.5% of taxes (collected according to the ex-factory tax), while the tax rate for imported Western goods in our industry is 55%. Although our association has notified the industry to refuse to sell smuggled goods, the woolen cloth, silk, and cotton cloth industries have always sold them, so if we want to prevent smuggling, these two industries must stop selling them, or cooperate with our industry, which may be effective. Fellow members of our association have repeatedly suggested to the association that we conduct a thorough investigation of the products of domestic woolen cloth factories, that the authorities should send resident factory commissioners to check foreign factory export goods according to the methods of cigarette factories, and that goods from Manchuria and Mongolia should not be allowed to be transshipped; if they want to be transshipped, they should be handled in the same way as imported Western goods, and through bills of lading should not be given special rights. The association will submit a request on these three principles when it next meets with the Inspector of Customs. Recently, it was heard that goods from a certain Japanese factory were specially allowed to be released tax-free. The industry is currently investigating the truth to correct it.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry of Finance to Request the Abolition of Tea Transit Tax 106

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, stating, "To the esteemed officials of the Ministry of Finance: This month, the Tea Trade Association of this city sent a letter stating that tea is a major national product and a natural product. Internally, it is a daily necessity for the people, and externally, it is a means of promoting national products and recovering profits. Since foreign teas from Japan and India have competed in the international market, the sales volume of Chinese tea has gradually been eliminated, and it has become a spent force. In the past, tea industry groups in various places repeatedly requested the Ministry of Finance to implement tax exemption in advance and gradually reduce the burden. In April of last year, the Ministry of Finance issued a reply with Customs Document No. 590, stating, 'We have received your presentation and understand. We have presented the item of transit tax to the Executive Yuan for submission to the Central Political Committee for approval, and it will be implemented on a scheduled basis. The transit tax that should be paid for tea sold domestically will be suspended at the same time as other local goods, and it is not appropriate to abolish it in advance, which would involve disputes. Please be informed accordingly.' However, it has not been implemented for a long time. On March 22 this year, the Third General Assembly of the Tea Technology Discussion Conference of the Agricultural Department of the National Economic Committee was jointly decided by tea experts from various places to exempt taxes in advance, and they requested the Ministry of Finance and the Executive Yuan to help with relief. They requested that the original plan be investigated and that taxes be exempted as soon as possible. To this day, there has been no effect. The industry association stated that due to frequent floods and banditry in recent years, the tea industry has suffered great damage, and many have been reduced to bankruptcy. Even if they barely maintain the status quo, they feel exhausted. Therefore, we propose to forward the request to the Ministry of Finance to investigate the original plan of Customs Document No. 590 of the 24th year and to promptly exempt the domestic transit tax on tea in advance, implement tax exemption, reduce the burden, and maintain the national tea industry, which would be greatly beneficial." Upon arrival at the meeting, it was found that the abolition of the transit tax was previously hindered by the increase in import tax to offset it. It was planned to change the income tax to offset it, and the discussion lasted for years, so the date was delayed. Now that the income tax has been set to be held within this year, according to recent news reports, it seems to be very promising. In the future, the tax source for compensation has been secured, and tea is a special domestic product that urgently needs support. It is reasonable to cable your department to review and approve the request of the association, immediately abolish the transit tax on a scheduled basis, reduce costs, and facilitate sales. [We] would be exceedingly grateful. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce respectfully submits this."

On the 19th, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, stating, "To the esteemed officials of the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance: Chen Kaiqing's letter states that the Customs re-seized and punished a jadeite boulder that had already been taxed and fined. It seems difficult to speculate with common sense. Since the stone was seized, it has been over a year. The losses suffered as a result are enormous, and the mental anguish is indescribable. Bureau of Commodity Inspection to Convene Silk Factory Conference Today 108

To Discuss the Implementation of Grade Inspection Methods for Raw Silk Products; Representatives from Shanghai, Zhejiang, and Wuxi Silk Factories Are All Preparing to Attend

After receiving instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to prepare for the export commodity grade inspection of raw silk, the Shanghai Bureau of Commodity Inspection has been prepared by Miao Zhongxiu, Director of the Sericulture Group, etc. The key points and procedures for raw silk grade inspection have been formulated and sent to various silk factories and silk industry organizations for reference, and will be implemented on July 1. In order to facilitate implementation, a meeting of representatives from the industry associations of silk factories in Shanghai, Zhejiang, and Wuxi will be convened at 2:00 PM today in the Bureau's conference room at the China Bank warehouse in Beinicheng Bridge to discuss implementation methods. According to the representatives, the draft of the raw silk export grade inspection standards formulated by the Bureau of Commodity Inspection adopts the method of inspecting Japanese silk in the American market. Because of the different machinery in China's silk factories, the silkworm varieties have not yet been unified, and the workers' skills have not been properly trained, it will be difficult to implement universally after implementation. At the meeting, the reasons for the difficulties and obstacles will be reported in detail to facilitate discussion in the long term.

General Bureau for the Production and Sale of Party and National Flags Replies to the Joint Association of Special District Citizens 112

Details the Circumstances of Price Setting

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Joint Association, according to a letter from the 46th District Branch of the Association, criticized the high price of the Party and National Flag and forwarded the letter to the General Bureau for the Production and Sale of Party and National Flags, instructing it to reduce the price within the possible range. Now it is known that the Bureau has replied based on the facts. The original letter stated: "In reply, we have received your letter of June 18 and learned that the 46th District Branch of your association believes that the current price of the flags set by our Bureau is too high and requested your association to forward it to the Party and government organs to order our Bureau to reduce the price. Therefore, your association instructed our Bureau to reduce the price within the possible range to facilitate promotion. After reading it, we deeply admire your insight and clear observation. Because your branch has already recognized that the flag manufacturing technology sold by our Bureau is indeed more advanced than that sold by merchants in the past, and as for reducing the price, there is no evidence that the current price of the flag is indeed higher than that sold by merchants in the past. What is said is not necessarily flattering, but it is ultimately unavoidable by those who know. If the current price of the flag is the same as that sold by merchants in the past, then the fact that the technology has improved will become the target of reducing the price. Rewarding and punishing are reversed, knowing that it is unfair, but with the letter request, it is inevitable to inquire whether there is a possible range for reducing the price. Therefore, based on the facts, we specially describe the price setting process for your association. Since our Bureau was granted the power to produce and sell the Party and National Flag by the Central Party Department and the Ministry of the Interior, we have been working hard to research the suitability of flag making for printing and dyeing regulations under the supervision of personnel from the Party and government organs. The time and expense wasted were extremely difficult. Later, when the research was completed, we listed the value of the cost in detail according to the production and sales procedures and requested the Central Party Department to set the selling price. At that time, the flag price on the market, taking size 6 as an example, was 2 yuan 40 cents to 2 yuan 80 cents per flag. The Central Party Department cared about the people's difficulties and had already taken this into consideration, so it reviewed the cost and set the initial price at 2 yuan 20 cents per flag. The initial pricing was more than 10% lower than the inflated price of pieced and discolored flags sold on the market. Later, more ground feet were added, and then the public price was set at 2 yuan per flag. The current price is nearly 30% lower than the inflated price of pieced and discolored flags sold on the market. The thin profit is well known to the pricing officials. If the actual sales volume is different from the expected volume, the profit revenue will not only be insufficient to compensate for the loss of research, but also may not be able to balance the current expenditure. In the past few months, there have been many setbacks in flag making and flag sales, and the losses have already been a fact. Mayor Wu believes that the promotion of the Party and National Flag is enough to awaken the public's awareness of cherishing the national flag, and also knows that our Bureau is experiencing difficulties, which is indeed true. Therefore, he invited your association and other parks to organize the Party and National Flag Promotion Committee, relying on your great support and assistance, hoping to sell more than the fixed amount and make up for the previous losses. Unexpectedly, the 46th District Branch of your association did not investigate the facts and relied on likes and dislikes to take this opportunity to wantonly attack and criticize. Therefore, regardless of whether the current flag price is nearly 30% lower than the pieced and discolored flags sold on the market in the past, even if the current flag price is indeed higher than that sold by merchants in the past, the infamous name of unscrupulous merchants should not be added to our Bureau, which has no right to set the price. Fortunately, your association is wise and was not misled, and we are deeply grateful for your concern. We have truthfully replied. If you are prepared to issue an official letter, send a representative to visit our Bureau, and have further inquiries, we will naturally be happy to receive your guidance."

North Station Trains Were Blocked Yesterday Morning; Normalcy Resumed at 2:00 PM in the Afternoon 114

The North Station trains on both the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou lines were blocked yesterday morning, causing some trains to fail to depart on time. Sino-British Wireless Telephone to Officially Operate in Autumn; Ministry of Communications Negotiating Communication Contract with British Side; Sino-American and Sino-Philippine Communication Difficult to Achieve in Short Term 115

The Sino-British wireless telephone, since the Ministry of Communications ordered the International Radio Station to start preparing last year, has been several months. The International Radio Station in Sassoon Building, Renji Road, Shanghai, has used the terminal of the Liuhang Reporting Station to hold several trial conversations with the London Radio Station in the United Kingdom, and the results have been quite good. In order to make the technology more skilled, two trials are still held every week, each lasting 15 minutes, and the results are better than before. As for the formal communication procedures, the Ministry of Communications has directly contacted the British side to proceed and has drafted a communication contract and sent it to the British side to solicit opinions. According to a reporter from Xin Xin She, the International Radio Station is only responsible for all technical aspects of Sino-British communication. As for the formal communication negotiation matters, the Ministry of Communications directly discusses with the British side, so the communication date is still to be decided by the Ministry of Communications. At present, the technical aspects are all ready, and all other procedures are expected to be completed in the shortest time. It is expected that formal communication will be possible in the autumn of this year. As for Sino-American communication, the equipment has also been arranged, but because the day and night time between the two countries is opposite, the business hours are still to be discussed, and it is difficult to achieve for the time being. Sino-Philippine communication has been virtually suspended because the company responsible on the Philippine side has not yet been decided.

County Government to Reorganize District, Township, and Town Offices; Implemented Uniformly Starting Yesterday 117

The Shanghai County Government recently received an order from the Songjiang District Commissioner's Office, stating that district, township, and town offices are lower-level cadres under the command of the county government to implement government orders. If they can be sound, they can achieve the effect of the body using arms and fingers. The county government then followed the reorganization plan and ordered all districts to comply with it. District office staff and township and town chiefs should uniformly wear yellow Zhongshan suits and soft-brimmed military caps. The township and town offices should hang the Party and National Flag, Sun Yat-sen's portrait, and Chiang Kai-shek's portrait in the auditorium or in the middle of the office. County Government Abolishes Fishery Tax in This County Under Order 118

The Shanghai County Government has now received an order from the Provincial Government stating that the types of miscellaneous taxes and levies on agricultural land vary from county to county, and the names are different. There have been many abuses in the collection over the years, and the amount is too small, similar to harsh miscellaneous taxes. The Department of Finance previously issued a circular to each county to investigate and statistics, list and submit to the government for approval to abolish. The county should abolish one type of miscellaneous tax, the fishery tax, starting from the 25th year (1936). The collection should be stopped immediately. Except for old debts from previous years, which are allowed to continue to be repaid, if any private collection in the name of borrowing is still found, it will be dealt with strictly according to law. County Governor Ye has ordered the land tax collection office of the county government to stop the collection from this year.

The boy scout labor service in this city was held yesterday in the city center. Despite the rain and wet ground in the early morning, the boy scouts were not daunted at all, and their spirit was admirable. They worked hard all day and completed one road, which truly demonstrated the vigor of Shanghai's youth. Details of the situation are recorded below:

Participating Boy Scouts

At 7 a.m. yesterday morning, boy scouts from various schools and organizations, following orders, arrived at the site to register. They included Minsheng, Minli, Jinghua, Jinrong, Private Shanghai Middle School, City North, Guangong, Yucai, Daozhong, YMCA, City Chamber of Commerce, Sino-French, Qingnian, Tongyi, Shaoniantuan, Xiangxing, Datong, the Girls' Middle School of the Municipal Council, Huafeng, Renyi, Nanyang, Danhua, Yangjing, Qinghua, Siyu, Guangdong, Quanzhang, Post Office No. 2, Lida, Minguang, Gongyi, Dian, He'an, and other primary and secondary school groups, as well as more than eighty social groups, totaling two thousand boy and girl scouts. Mayor Breaks Ground

At 8 a.m. sharp, Director Pan Gongzhan, representing Mayor Wu, arrived at the site in military uniform and performed the groundbreaking ceremony. Cannons were fired for the groundbreaking, and the ceremony was simple and solemn. After the ceremony, the staff directed the work of each group, distributed tools to each person, and assigned sections of the area. Tea and water were provided by the Municipal Government and the kitchens of various bureaus at the Municipal Government Auditorium and the dining area. At 1 p.m. in the afternoon, the weather cleared up, and spirits were even higher. Many citizens came to watch.

Work Achievements

Many hands make light work. Ribbon Cutting for Opening

As the clock struck five, all the boy scouts were assembled and lined up along the road. Tong Hangbai, a standing director of the council, inspected each road, and then the ribbon cutting ceremony was held on Zhirenyong Road to open it to traffic. Mr. Tong Hangbai rode in a car of the City Chamber of Commerce around the road for a week. All the boy scouts cheered and jumped with joy, forgetting their fatigue, and happily returned home by car, with songs still resounding in their mouths.

Chinese-owned Spindles Gradually Decrease, Yarn Industry's Future Increasingly Difficult, Japanese Yarn Factories Increase Spindles and Operate Day and Night, Factories in North China Still Shut Down, Requesting Relief 124

The Chinese-owned textile factories have been affected by the economic downturn in recent years, and financial institutions have tightened loans, resulting in a gradual decrease in spindles. The damage is so deep that it is already in a difficult situation. The Japanese-owned yarn factories, which hold a superior position in China, are prospering, and the Chinese yarn factories in North China are still shut down. The reporter of the Dagong News Agency reported on the situation as follows:

A Glimpse of the Current Situation of Chinese-owned Yarn Factories

According to a leader in the yarn industry, there are a total of twenty-four textile factories established by Chinese in various parts of the country, with approximately 2.7 million spindles. Since the Chinese yarn industry has been affected by the economic downturn in recent years, financial institutions have generally adopted a tight policy for loan recovery, because of the decline in industry, and have taken a very small grip on loans. As a result, the yarn industry has suffered a fatal blow in terms of economic flow. Factories that have stopped or reduced work have emerged one after another. Until now, not only is it difficult to restore vitality, but each factory is still reducing the number of spindles, starting and stopping work frequently, and taking holidays and stopping work for more than one-third of the time each month, struggling in the raging waves. The result of our only national industry is something that has never been dreamed of.

Japanese Textile Factories Increase Number of Spindles

The Japanese-owned yarn factories in China are located in Shanghai, Qingdao, and Hankou, with 2.45 million spindles. In Tianjin, they have also acquired our Yuyuan and Yuda yarn factories and are expanding significantly. The number of spindles is planned to be temporarily set at 600,000. Recently, the Shanghai Internal and External Cotton, Nihua, Gongda, Toyota, Shanghai and other factories have increased the number of spindles by 150,000 since last month, operating day and night, and shipping goods out in an extremely busy manner. However, since smuggled cotton cloth products have penetrated into various ports in Central China, yarn sales have also been slightly affected.

Factories in Tianjin Still Shut Down

The Yuda and Yuyuan factories in Tianjin owned by Chinese were acquired by Japanese and rebuilt and expanded. The Beiyang Yarn Factory was also transferred to Japanese ownership, and it is heard that the deal has been completed. However, the Chinese-owned yarn factories in North China are actually only Hengyuan, Laicheng, and three others. Due to capital constraints, they have not yet started work. The manufacturers have held meetings and telegraphed the Ministry of Industry for relief. They also plan to borrow money from local banks to plan for progress.
