Concession Health Authorities Discuss the Original Intent of Milk Tuberculosis Testing, Preventing Glandular Tuberculosis and Bone Tuberculosis in Children 128

Regarding the improvement of the quality of milk in this port and the Municipal Council's encouragement of testing cattle for tuberculosis, the measures taken by the health authorities of the concession have been reported in the press. Now, according to a statement by a person from the health authorities of the Public Concession, public opinion is still divided on the implementation of this new policy. Those who aim high and far say that Shanghai is far behind other major cities in terms of milk supply, and that milk should not be divided into grades at all, and only the best should be allowed to be sold. In fact, this kind of argument is still beyond the times and has not yet reached the time for implementation. Furthermore, the tuberculosis bacteria contained in milk are very different from human tuberculosis bacteria, and there is no need to discuss them together. The reason why the health authorities must encourage the testing of cattle for tuberculosis is, firstly, to maintain the health of livestock, and secondly, to hope to eliminate the source of tuberculosis in children's glands and bones from bovine tuberculosis bacteria. As for human tuberculosis, the problem is very complicated, and its relationship with milk is very small. The first method of prevention is to avoid contact with patients with pulmonary tuberculosis, and there is no need to worry about whether the milk has been tested. Furthermore, in May, three groups of cattle, totaling 110 heads, were tested for tuberculosis by the Municipal Council, and one head showed a positive reaction and was immediately isolated.

High Tide in the Huangpu River Yesterday Morning 133

Quantity Exceeded the Shanghai Observatory Prediction, Low-Lying Roads Were Inundated with Backflow

The weather in this port this year has been particularly rainy and less sunny, and the climate is very cool. Although it has turned hot a few days ago, it has cooled down again since the 19th, and the sky is overcast. That night, there was a torrential downpour, and it rained intermittently all day the day before yesterday. Until yesterday, although it was the summer solstice, it was still cloudy and sunny, with clouds drifting past. The Huangpu River tide occurred again last night. At 1:23 a.m. yesterday, the quantity suddenly broke out as scheduled, exceeding the forecast of eleven feet, three inches, and five minutes. According to the investigation, the reason for the excess was due to the bad weather. When the outbreak started, the low-lying roads were inundated with backflow from the sewers, including the intersection of Gansu Road and Alabaster Road, the side of Yong'an Company on Zhejiang Road, and the front of China Sales Company on Sichuan Road. The high tide had subsided after 9 a.m. yesterday.

Yangtze Silver Company

The Case of Suing the Vienna Dance Hall, the Original Plaintiff Was Ruled to Be Rejected 138

According to Article 450, Paragraph 2 of the Civil Code, the Custom Should Be Followed, The Request for Rent Increase Reached More Than Three Times the Original Rent, Resulting in Failure to Evict

The Vienna Flower Dance Hall at No. 6 Dihua Road, Jing'an Temple Road, occupies an area of more than five acres. It was rented from the Yangtze Silver Company at No. 9 Avenue Edward VII on June 1 of the Republic of China. There was a contract with a limit of six months, and the monthly rent was 700 yuan. However, since the expiration on November 30 of the same year, Vienna has continued to rent, but no formal contract has been renewed. Recently, the Yangtze Silver Company entrusted a lawyer on March 30 to send a letter to the dance hall, limiting it to returning the rented land before May 21. Because the Vienna Dance Hall refused, the Yangtze Silver Company filed a lawsuit against the Vienna Dance Hall in the Civil Court of the First Special District Court, requesting that the defendant be ordered to return the rented land and bear all litigation costs. Lawyers Yan Chen and Jiang Baoyi argued that according to Article 450, Paragraph 2 of the Civil Code, "For an indefinite lease contract, although temporary amendments may be made, the custom that is beneficial to the lessee should be followed." According to Shanghai custom, the lessor can only claim termination of the contract if the lessee is in arrears of rent for three months or more, or if the lessor recovers it for its own use. The defendant has never been in arrears of rent, and the plaintiff has not stated that it is recovering it for its own use, only requesting to recover the rented land, which is obviously contrary to the above-mentioned custom. Moreover, the defendant has the right to use the plaintiff's land. According to Article 832 of the Civil Code, the plaintiff can only revoke the right of superficies if the arrears of land rent reach the total amount of two years. Therefore, the plaintiff's claim has no reason. Moreover, the filing of this case is actually caused by the plaintiff's failure to evict the increase in rent. In the past, the plaintiff would ask to increase the rent to more than three times the original land rent. In this autumn of a hundred industries, the defendant could not afford it. Repeated consultations failed to yield any results. The plaintiff ordered to return the rented land and even claimed that the defendant's investment in the construction and decoration of the rented land was more than 100,000 yuan. It has only been in operation for more than two years, and the profits have been extremely small. Now the plaintiff's claim is not in accordance with the law, it is completely a threat to increase the rent, it is really unreasonable, and the plaintiff's lawsuit should be rejected, and the litigation fees should be borne. This case has been concluded after being summoned by the First Special Court. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Yuhai announced the judgment: The main text of the plaintiff's lawsuit was rejected, and the litigation fees were borne by the plaintiff.

Seventh Day of the Hygiene Campaign: Children's Speech Final Held Yesterday 139

Speech Finals

Chairman Director Li, (represented by Zhou), performed the rituals, followed by a report on the progress of the speech competition. Then, the speech final began. Ten children, including Zhang Yinchan from Qingxin, participated. Judges Zhou Guobao, Zhu Jiarang, Wu Ya, (Yan Wenkai represented) Pan Gongzhan, (Zhang Meisong represented) Zhang Binghui, and Wu Zhongyao determined the rankings. Qingxin's Zhang Yinchan (an eight-year-old girl) won first place with the topic "How to Develop Good Hygiene Habits in Children." Wan Zhuda Cong won second place (topic: "Children's Health"), and Zhu Chuanfang from Jingxiong won third place (topic: "How to Protect Our Teeth"). Section Chief Shen presented them with silver tripods and silver shields, donated by Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Zhu Jiahe, respectively. Li Meirong from Jing'an and Ke Reng were among the seven other participants who were also awarded silver shields and silver cups for encouragement.

Weightlifting Competition

The citizens' weightlifting competition was held at the Children's Living Park yesterday at 2:00 PM. The People's Education Center hired Ye Liang and Weng Jiankang from the Municipal National Arts Center to serve as judges. Participants included twelve in the lightweight division, such as Ding Daxiong and Zha Dengkui, eleven in the light middleweight division, such as Lin Hai and Zhu Guangyao, eight in the middleweight division, such as Qi Mugen and Pin Jigang, three in the light heavyweight division, such as Zhang Wenxiang, and one in the heavyweight division, Chang Qun. Chang Guan-qun won the heavyweight title with 689 pounds, the light heavyweight winner lifted 552 pounds, the second-place winner Yao Tai lifted 546 pounds, and the third-place winner Zhu De lifted 334 pounds. Lu Jigang won first place in the middleweight division with 516 pounds, followed by Bo Yu in second place with 486 pounds, and Chen Linchang in third place with 486 pounds. Chen Jinsheng won first place in the light middleweight division with 480 pounds, followed by Bo Yinsheng in second place with 462 pounds, and Cheng Yuzhen in third place with 462 pounds. Hua Fengchun won first place in the lightweight division with 402 pounds, followed by Ding Daxiong in second place with 402 pounds, and Zhang Jinshan in third place with 286 pounds. Chang Guanqun's weightlifting record exceeded the selection competition for the World Games athletes. His personal record was 680 pounds.

Prosecutor Reprimands Chen Anhe, Habitual Pigeon Release Practitioner 145

Jin Feng Recounts Past Hardships and Joys: Official Deals with Zhang Shi's Adoption by Contract

Zhang Shi, a woman from Chuansha residing on Jiangyin Street in Xiaoximen, adopted Jin Feng, the eight-year-old daughter of Chen Anhe, a leather craftsman from Jiangbei and neighbor, as her adopted daughter last year. At that time, she gave him 16 yuan for milk and food expenses. After Jin Feng entered her household, she told her that she had been sold by her father four times in the name of adoption. One was to a family of opera singers, one to a tailor shop, and one to people from her hometown. This was the last time. When Zhang Shi heard this, she feared that Chen Anhe would continue this practice and entice her to run away, resulting in the loss of both person and money. Therefore, she considered moving to be a good strategy and sent Jin Feng to her aunt in Chuansha to prevent any evil plans. Unexpectedly, Chen Anhe's evil plans failed, and he repeatedly extorted money from Zhang Shi, falsely accusing her of selling the girl and demanding 200 yuan. Zhang Shi reported this to the police, who arrested him at the Wenmiao Road Police Station and sent him to the local court. Zhang Shi went to Chuansha to bring the girl to the court. Yesterday, Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu held a preliminary hearing. The girl went to court and recounted the above situation, saying that she had suffered greatly in Chen's house, endured hunger, and was only given a bowl of cold fruit to fill her stomach. Now, she lived like a treasure in her foster mother's house and did not want to leave. The prosecutor severely reprimanded Chen Anhe, ordering him not to habitually release pigeons, harass, or extort money. Since Jin Feng was adopted by Zhang Shi according to the contract, the court allowed Zhang Shi to take her back to raise her.

The police officers on patrol sent him to the General Hospital, but the treatment was ineffective and he died shortly after.

Robbers Hire Car to Steal Money 147

At about 10:00 PM last night, three men suddenly hired a car from the Xiang Sheng Car Company on Min Ti Ni Yin Road in the French Concession and went to Lincoln Road in western Shanghai. The accounting office contacted a chauffeur surnamed Jia, who drove a rental car with Concession license plate number 18549 to the destination. Unexpectedly, the three passengers took out pistols, ordered him not to make a sound, and robbed the chauffeur of 10 yuan in French currency from his pocket. The three then got out of the car and fled. The chauffeur shouted loudly for help, but the Jing'an Temple Police Station officers who arrived on the scene after hearing the shouts fired a shot into the darkness. But unfortunately, the robbers had already disappeared.

Robbers Snatch Gold Earrings, Open Fire in Desperation and Wound Hands and Faces 148

Shi Yang and Yu Sun Simultaneously Injured and Sent to Hospital

Shi Yang, a 41-year-old woman, and Yu Sun, a 31-year-old woman from Nanjing, lived at No. 121, known as 24 Jiantou, on Rihui Bridge, Xiaosha Ferry Road. They each set up a miscellaneous goods stall at the entrance to earn a meager profit. Due to their frugality, they had some savings. Therefore, both women had gold earrings made in the bank. Unexpectedly, they were targeted by bandits. At about 9:00 PM last night, as the two women were packing up at their stalls at the entrance, three or four bandits suddenly came and tore off the earrings from both of them, intending to flee. Both women suffered severe pain, and upon seeing their gold jewelry being robbed, they cried out in unison and desperately grabbed the robbers. At that time, the bandits had not gone far. Hearing the cries, they panicked and immediately fired two shots before fleeing. One bullet hit Shi Yang's hand, and the other hit Yu Sun's face. By the time the police received the report and arrived, it was too late. They first sent the two women to the hospital for treatment and then pursued the bandits.

Sick Woman Commits Suicide with Scissors 149

Lin Sun Dejected Due to Prolonged Illness: Family Carelessness Leads to Tragedy

Lin Sun, a 30-year-old woman, married Lin Xiaoxiang, a cook, and lived with him at No. 12, Man Yang Li, on Dongyouheng Road. However, Lin Sun was weak and ill, taking medicine all year round. Despite the diagnosis and treatment by Chinese and Western doctors, the medicine was ineffective and did not cure her chronic illness. Therefore, Lin Sun often complained and harbored thoughts of death. However, her family was very vigilant, so there were no accidents. Unexpectedly, yesterday afternoon, she took advantage of the family's inattention and suddenly grabbed a pair of scissors from the table and frantically slashed her throat. Immediately, blood flowed like a waterfall, and she collapsed on the bed. By the time the family discovered it, she was already on her last breath. They rushed her to the hospital for treatment, but due to her long illness and the severity of her injuries, she could not be saved and died at 5:00 PM.

Phonograph Factory Employee Arrested for Stealing Ten Records 150

Yao Shiru, a 24-year-old Suzhou native living at No. 1, Yong'an Li, Jiajiadu in the South City, worked as an employee at the Pathé Phonograph and Record Factory, a French company located at No. 1099, Xujiahui Road in the French Concession. At 5:00 PM on the 19th of this month, Yao stole ten finished records from the factory, hid them on his body, and left the factory. He was discovered by a guard, who found the records, informed the accounting office, and reported to the French Police Station. A detective was dispatched to arrest Yao. The next day, he was sent to the Second Special Court, Eighth Criminal Division. Attorney Chen Ming, from the Police Affairs Office, described the case and requested an extension for investigation, before asking for a trial. Then, Detective Xu Daorong reported the arrest of the defendant and submitted the evidence to the case. After the judge confirmed the report and questioned the defendant, permission was granted to postpone the hearing. Yao was ordered to provide a 500 yuan guarantee for attending the hearing when summoned. Without a guarantee, he was detained.

Smuggling Opium Seized 151

Water Patrol Team Receives Confidential Tip

Kong Zhaorong, a patrol officer of the Third Detachment of the Shanghai City Patrol, received a confidential tip that a large quantity of opium was being smuggled into Shanghai. He immediately led the police to conduct a thorough inspection in his jurisdiction yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. At the Japan Concession port, they saw a vessel resembling a rice boat (City License No. 16775) approaching. Suspecting its behavior, they ordered it to stop and boarded the ship to search it. They discovered seven large packages of opium (50 small packages in each) and five small packages, totaling 355 taels, as well as two opium cakes. The three crew members were arrested and interrogated. They identified themselves as Hu A'er (31 years old, Minhang native), Yang Baisheng (35 years old, Minhang native), and A San (39 years old, Minhang native). They confirmed that the captain of the vessel had escaped. They confessed to selling opium. The three crew members, along with the opium, have been sent to the General Detachment and transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Zhang Jianming Dies After Mistakenly Eating Puffer Fish Roe 153

Deadly Poisoning Due to Insufficient Washing: Medical Treatment Too Late to Save Him

Zhang Jianming, a 48-year-old Suzhou native, lived at No. 225, Kaifeng Road, and worked as a manager at the Xiangtai Silk Weaving Factory on Binyuan Road in this city. Yesterday afternoon, Zhang obtained several puffer fish from the market and instructed the cook at home to prepare them carefully. Unexpectedly, the fish were not washed thoroughly, and some roe was left behind. Zhang did not notice it at the time and mistakenly ate it. Soon after, he was poisoned. Upon seeing this, his family quickly sent him to the hospital for treatment. However, it was too late, and he died at 9:00 PM. His body has been sent to the coroner's office and will be reported to the court for examination.

Second Annual Meeting of the Personnel Management Society 155

Shen Jiucheng and Xiang Kangyuan Elected as Directors

The Chinese Personnel Management Society has been established for over two years. For the purpose of reviewing the past and encouraging the future, the second annual meeting was held yesterday (21st) afternoon at the Huahai Hotel of the China Vocational Education Society. More than forty members attended, including Pan Yangyao, He Qingru, Shi Jiuyun, Gu Bingyuan, Huang Jingwan, Yang Chongxun, Wu Zongwen, Zhou Mengyun, Lou Wenzhou, Wang Fugang, Ka Zongyuan, Huang Erxi, Chen Shouhe, Zhu Tongzhou, Gu Junquan, Shen Qinwu, Zhang Mingrong, Wen Chonglu, Xu Xingbai, Zhou Xinhao, Zhang Yiru, He Zhentang, and Su Changyan. He Qingru chaired the meeting, Duan Yaoxiang provided stenographic recording, and after performing the rituals, Chairman He Qingru first gave a report (excerpt): Today is the second anniversary of the Personnel Management Society. Members gather together to discuss the affairs of the association and to plan for its development. Details of the association's affairs have been detailed in the personnel management publications that were distributed today. Aside from the fact that the publications were discontinued due to the environment, the number of individual members has increased by more than 200, and the number of group members has also increased by more than 10. Other activities, such as the organization of visits to industrial and commercial organizations, have been conducted ten times, with ten to twenty people participating each time, and the results have been very good. In terms of publications, the Personnel Management Monthly is published every month. Although the scope is small, it is still a pioneering effort in China and can penetrate into the interior, serving as a source of research. Due to time constraints, there are still many association affairs to be discussed. I will not say more. Then, Pan Yangyao gave a speech, stating that the importance of personnel management is that one should pay attention to personnel management in order to seek the soundness and development of the organization. The defects of today's organizations are all due to the lack of attention to personnel management. I have traveled to more than ten counties in northern Jiangsu, and the failure of the supervisory sites is also due to this. If one can pay attention, it will not be so. Finally, he also explained the key points for various organizations to prevent corruption: leaders should often meet with subordinates, ensure that all subordinates have a comfortable life, and engage in proper entertainment. The decline of today's youth is the responsibility of the leaders, not the fault of the youth. The youth are like blank paper, and when they enter society, they have no bad habits, which are all caused by the environment. Therefore, when an organization uses people, it should first emphasize selection, and then enable them to practice proper entertainment and stabilize their lives. This is the only good way to prevent corruption. Today, I am very happy to be able to participate in the grand meeting and report my humble opinions. Subsequently, Shi Jiuyun and Gu Bingyuan gave speeches, elaborating on the promotion of corruption prevention and consumer cooperation among organizations, especially the promotion of welfare undertakings. Discussions then began: [Resolution to Establish a Personnel Guidance Department] Resolved: Approved in principle. The name and methods will be discussed by the Board of Directors. [Discussion on the Regulations of the Corruption Prevention Committee] Resolved: Passed. [The number of directors can be increased to nine, with three alternate directors] Resolved: Passed. Subsequently, the election was held. Xiang Kangyuan, Shi Jiuyun, Gu Bingyuan, and Shen Jiucheng were elected as new directors. Zhang Sumin, Zhang Yunbao, and Wang Weiyin were elected as alternate directors. Afterwards, refreshments were served, photos were taken, and the meeting was adjourned.

It was decided to notify all members to refuse to buy smuggled goods. The Municipal Party Department issued an order to form a New Life Service Corps within a specific timeframe. It was decided that all executive committee members would serve as organizing committee members and actively promote the effort. Finally, other important matters were discussed before the meeting adjourned. On the same day, another meeting of the supervisory committee was held, attended by Wang Zaiyou, Gu Zhujun, and Zhang Bingxin. They mutually elected Wang Youzong as chief supervisor, followed by the discussion of several routine matters before adjourning, and the details were submitted to the relevant higher authorities for record.

Minutes of the Executive and Supervisory Committee Meeting of the Kerosene Industry Guild 160

The Shanghai Municipal Kerosene Industry Guild, located on Old Baidu Street, Nanshi, convened its first joint executive and supervisory committee meeting of the third session yesterday. Ten committee members attended, and Chai Linsheng was publicly elected as chairman, with Chen Xi serving as recorder. After formal greetings, (A) matters reported included receiving a certificate of commendation for promoting education and one instruction from the Municipal Party Department, two letters from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and two other documents. Regarding how to handle the Municipal Party Department's instruction to organize a New Movement Labor Service Corps, it was decided to reply to the New Movement Promotion Association. Regarding the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's request for information on methods to inspect smuggled goods for reference, it was decided to reply to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating the guild's opinions. Regarding the request from Xie Hexiang Western Company and Meikang Western Company to join the guild as members, it was decided to send letters of inquiry to both companies. Regarding the election of standing committee members for the current session and the mutual election of a chairman, Chai Linsheng, Chen Yongnian, and Xie Boshe were elected as standing committee members, and Chai Linsheng was mutually elected as chairman. Regarding the reporting of the election situation and the election of officials for the current session to higher authorities, it was decided to have the documentation department handle it. The meeting then adjourned.

Wu Rongtai Flower Powder Shop Announces Closure and Seeks a Buyer 161

According to Xin Xin News Agency, the Huajin Lane area of Shanxi Road, where flower powder shops are concentrated, has recently been affected by the city's economic downturn, resulting in occasional closures. Now, Wu Rongtai Flower Powder Shop, unable to sustain operations, has announced its closure and has entrusted attorney Feng Meixue to represent them in settling accounts and seeking a buyer. Their announcement states: "We, the aforementioned parties, hereby declare that our shop, Wu Rongtai, has been operating in Huajin Lane on Sanma Road for over twenty years. Due to the current state of business, we are unable to continue operations. We have engaged an attorney to represent us in settling accounts. All creditors are requested to register their claims with the attorney's office within two weeks. Claims submitted after the deadline will be subject to legal action. All assets and goods of our shop are also being offered for sale. We hereby announce this for public awareness."

Huasheng Electric Fans Enjoy Strong Sales 162

The various electric fans produced by the Huasheng factory have seen increasing sales. New businesses in Shanghai this year, such as the Daxin Company, the Shanghai Fish Market, and the Dagong Daily, have all installed fans supplied by the factory. The direct current fans used on the Sanbei Shipping Company's ships are also entirely manufactured by the factory. Therefore, although foreign-made fans are being sold at reduced prices, Chinese people, with their strong sense of patriotism, are ignoring them.

Cai Jinjun's Radio Address: Hygiene Movement Must Be Practiced on the Ground 171

The Shen Shi News Agency reports that Cai Jinjun, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, at the invitation of the 15th Municipal Hygiene Movement, gave a radio address at the Municipal Government Radio Station in the city center at 5:30 PM on the 19th. The topic of his speech was "The Hygiene Movement Must Be Practiced on the Ground." The content was divided into six points: National Health and Revival; Hygiene and Practice; Summer and Hygiene; Attention to Diet; Simplicity, Neatness, and Cleanliness; and the People's Efforts and the Supervision of the Public Security Bureau. Director Cai's original speech is as follows:

"Dear fellow citizens of Shanghai, the topic of my radio address today is 'The Hygiene Movement Must Be Practiced on the Ground.' When it comes to the word 'hygiene,' I believe everyone must think it is an extremely common and familiar term. However, it is precisely because it is too common and too familiar that we often overlook its importance and greatness. It not only contains the meaning of protecting individual life but also bears the great mission of protecting the life of the entire nation. However, because the nation is a collection of individuals, to achieve national hygiene, we must first achieve personal hygiene. To seek national health, we must first seek individual health. Especially in this era of extremely fierce survival competition in the 20th century, maintaining the life of the nation is indeed not an easy task. If intelligence lags behind, we will naturally be eliminated. If physical strength is insufficient, the degree of danger is extremely significant. Especially our country, at this most critical juncture of crisis, whether the individual is healthy or not is the key to determining whether the entire nation will perish. We should not underestimate hygiene as just a very common term that we have long been accustomed to hearing. We must earnestly recognize its great mission of maintaining national life and reviving national glory. Look at Hitler's National Socialism, isn't it advocating national health and national hygiene, the 'superior race theory'? The physique of Germans is already very strong, but they still actively emphasize this point to save the nation and restore its pre-war status, and they are still working hard starting from individual health. How can we, our compatriots, not be called 'sick men of the East'? Isn't our country called the 'sick man of Asia'? If we want to wash away this shame, if we want to revive our nation, dear compatriots, we must quickly recognize the significance of this hygiene movement and put it into practice. So, how can we achieve the goal of hygiene? How can we be considered to have practiced hygiene work? The purpose of hygiene is to maintain health and promote health, that is, to passively prevent diseases and actively strengthen the body. As for how to do it to be hygienic and achieve this goal, I think Shanghai is the center of Chinese culture, and education is relatively widespread. Most citizens have received at least elementary education. On the one hand, they read hygiene courses in elementary schools for at least one or two years, and on the other hand, they can often obtain some knowledge about disease and health from newspapers and other sources. How to do it practically, we know, but all kinds of hygiene creeds, such as diet should be clean, clothes should be neat, air should be circulated, and daily life should be regular, these must be paid attention to at all times and places, and continuously every day. It is because of this reason that people feel impatient and neglect it, feel unable to persevere and interrupt it, and finally bad habits take root and good habits have no way to establish themselves. In fact, this difficulty is only a temporary phenomenon in the initial implementation. After a while, when habits are formed, not only will you not feel troublesome and trivial, but you will also feel very natural and casual, and you can easily conform to the rules without much effort. Therefore, I hope that all compatriots, if they have not yet understood the meaning of hygiene, quickly take advantage of this hygiene education and training. At this time of extreme national crisis, we must think about the future of our nation and the lives of ourselves, and quickly make a decision to eliminate the small obstacles in the initial implementation and establish a neat, clean, vigorous, and healthy life. At this final juncture, it is not permissible to talk about any theories, and hygiene is not a theory that can be talked about. Dear compatriots, we can only quickly put it into practice. The terrible summer season has already begun. This season of high summer and early autumn is the most active period for all germs, microorganisms, and harmful insects, and it is also the period of general attack by our enemies. Therefore, according to the statistics of any session, the mortality rate in this period must always account for the highest number. The weather is so hot, which is also intensifying the active power of the enemies. Dear compatriots, quickly find ways to consolidate our defense projects and quickly strive to eliminate our multiple enemies. The most important effort is to pay attention to diet because this is where all germs parasitize and reproduce, and it is also the only way for all enemies to attack our bodies. This of course requires caution at all times and attention everywhere. And what I hope for today is two things that are very practical and must be done. First, shops or hawkers on the streets, as long as they are places that sell food, must have complete hygienic facilities, all covered with iron gauze cages so that flies cannot reach them and dust cannot enter, which will cut off the source of the terrible cholera. Second, the kitchen of every household must be cleaned up very well. Do not buy back stale fish and meat just to save money. Do not buy too many vegetables that are needed every day and let them rot. The tableware used should be rinsed with boiling water frequently. Discarded garbage should also be dumped in a fixed and remote place. This will also reduce the base for germs to reside. As the saying goes, "All diseases enter through the mouth." During this hot summer, we must all pay extra attention. To sum it up, the basic principle of hygiene is to require cleanliness: food should be clean, clothes should be clean, the house should be clean, and the doorway and roads should also be clean. And to achieve cleanliness, there is a key method, which is to be neat. And to be neat, there is a key method, which is to be simple. For example, let's take our kitchen. To clean it up, we must put all the things, vegetables, salt, oil, fuel, bowls, etc., in a very neat order, in a fixed place. And to maintain a neat and orderly state forever, we must not pile up too many things that are not in use. If a family has only four people, then four sets of bowls and chopsticks are enough. When guests come, you can take them out temporarily. If there are many bowls and chopsticks piled up outside, it will easily become messy, and once it is messy, it will not be easy to clean. So, things should be simple, only when they are simple can they be neat, and only when they are neat can they be clean. I often hear some people say, "Hygiene is something that rich people talk about. Our lives are very simple, and it is not easy to talk about it." In fact, this reason is not sufficient because hygiene is not something difficult to do. As long as you pay attention a little bit and be more careful, make everything in life simple, neat, and clean, that's it. This is not only something that every citizen can do, but it is also easier to do the simpler the family. I never like to talk about any theories, and the hygiene movement does not need to talk about any theories. The significant meaning of this hygiene movement is to hope that all compatriots in Shanghai will deeply realize the great mission of hygiene in protecting individuals and reviving the nation, and at the same time be shocked by the severity of the situation, and strive to practice it earnestly. Public hygiene and personal hygiene are closely linked and mutually reinforcing. Therefore, the Public Security Bureau should definitely do its best to supervise the public hygiene of the city, and the most important thing is that every citizen should realize, act automatically, and persuade others as much as possible at any time and place to jointly complete this important mission. This is what I long for from all compatriots in Shanghai today. In this hot atmosphere, and with the utmost sincerity, I hope everyone takes care and wish you all health and happiness."

Fierce Competition Among Countries to Host the Next World Games 173

Netherlands Lists Eight Reasons Worth Noting

This World Games will be held in Germany starting on August 1st, and the venue for the next (12th) World Games will be decided at the closing ceremony. Countries are paying close attention to this issue, especially Finland and Japan are competing fiercely. As for the opinion of our country's sports authorities, they certainly hope that the next World Games can be held in China. If this goal cannot be achieved, it is considered better to be held in the Western District. Yesterday, our sports community received publicity materials from Finland for the competition for the venue of the next World Games, listing eight major reasons as follows:

Finland is a sports country.

Finland has sent personnel to participate in all World Games since 1903.

At the 1906 World Games in Athens, Finland won the first gold medal. In addition, in the track and field, wrestling, gymnastics, swimming, rowing, boxing, shooting, skiing, and skating events of the World Games, Finnish athletes have won a total of 62 World Games championships and gold medals, 60 silver medals, and 63 bronze medals.

In terms of total score calculation, Finland often occupies an advantage in the World Games. Assuming the ratio of population density is used, Finland is even more outstanding. If track and field is calculated, when the World Games were held in "Stockholm," Finland ranked second only to the United States. Since then, it has maintained its original position unchanged. In addition, at the 1911, 1920, and 1924 World Games, Finland won more medals in wrestling than the total won by other countries.

The 3.8 million people of Finland, united as one, support Finland's participation in the World Games. Its universality and number are unmatched by other countries.

Finland is a country that promoted sports very early and has specialized experience and knowledge in various sports. With the cooperation of government authorities and local authorities, if the next World Games are held in Finland, no shortcomings will be guaranteed in terms of economy, culture, sports, and any other aspect.

Finland is very close to the countries that have sent a large number of athletes to the World Games in the past, especially the travel expenses of European countries are more economical. Therefore, if it is held in Finland, athletes from various countries participating in the World Games will definitely be enthusiastic.

Finland is especially convenient for tourists, with lower exchange rates, lower living standards, beautiful scenery, eight islands, 60,000 lakes, midnight sun, and the Arftie seaside car road, which are unmatched by other countries.

School Survey: Overview of Shanghai Jewish School (Part Two) 189

— Hu Zuyin

Administrative Overview

The school's affairs are managed by the School Affairs Committee, which is organized by Jewish residents. The members are all honorary positions. The School Affairs Committee is responsible for the construction and repair of school buildings, as well as fundraising. All teaching and educational matters within the school are fully managed by the principal. The school's teachers and staff hold a meeting every two weeks to discuss issues related to improving teaching. According to the principal, this type of discussion meeting is very helpful for improving teaching.

The school's funding comes from approximately four sources: tuition fees, donations, subsidies, and gifts. The school principal declined to disclose the amount of each source of income. The tuition fees paid by students at all levels are the same. Special arrangements are in place for students from families with many children. In each family, the first student pays a monthly tuition fee of seven yuan, the second student pays a monthly tuition fee of five yuan, and the third, fourth, and subsequent students only pay a monthly tuition fee of three yuan. Monthly tuition fees must be paid in advance before attending classes. On the expenditure side, the salaries and wages of teachers and staff account for the majority, while equipment purchases account for only a small portion. Outside parties often make designated donations or gifts of food to the school for weak children to enjoy on a regular basis. For example, more than 160 children receive free lunch at the school, and the lunch fee is donated by the British industrialist Sir Ellis Kadoorie and his wife. Therefore, photos of the knight and his wife are hung in the dining room. The school doctor's remuneration is donated by Dr. Rosenzweig, a Russian. Another person donates cod liver oil and malt extract to weak children at the school free of charge. There are also two people who donate milk for undernourished children at the school to drink free of charge. Most of the books in the drawing room are donated by outsiders. In recent years, the market has been sluggish, and the school's external donations have also been affected. The budgeted revenue and expenditure for this year is still expected to be in deficit by a significant amount of between seven thousand and ten thousand yuan.

Teaching Highlights

Children at the school must study three languages: Hebrew (i.e., Jewish), English, and French. Subjects taught in Hebrew include reading, writing, translation, grammar, religion, history, and geography. The purpose of teaching Hebrew at the school is to enable Jewish children to recognize and understand the Bible and common prayers written in Hebrew. Teaching Jewish history focuses on children understanding the past history of their homeland and arousing children's awareness of the spirit of the Jewish nation. The maps used in teaching Jewish geography are the latest maps of Jewish holy sites and Palestine.

The purpose of Jewish children learning English is to adapt to modern society and be able to make a living using English. Subjects such as arithmetic, geometry, world history, geography, drawing, and handicrafts are all taught in English. The purpose of teaching French is to prepare middle school transfer students at the school to use it as a second foreign language when taking the Cambridge University entrance examination in England in the future. Syllabuses or key points have been prescribed for each subject, and teachers and students can work hard according to these outlines. The school uniquely lacks natural science and physical science experimental subjects, and only has simple observation courses that explain the life of plants and animals.

The school has regulations for the self-study work of students at all levels, but the amount varies at each level. When the school regulates students' self-study work, it takes into account students' health and curriculum distribution. Upper-grade students have approximately ninety minutes of self-study work each night, while lower-grade students rarely have self-study work each night. Students who are physically weak can be exempted from partial or full self-study work with a certificate from the school doctor. The school usually attaches great importance to various examinations.

Page 14

Economic Special Issue

The Development and Calculation of War Expenses (Continued) 190

— Zhang Yifan

"Four" The Development and Calculation of Expenses During Wartime

Since the Franco-Prussian War, the German Empire has often calculated the cost of future wars (Note 1) as a benchmark for expanding the amount of war reserve funds. Their estimation method was the second method mentioned above.

In 1890, the Prussian Minister of Finance and the President of the Imperial Bank, among others, estimated that the army and navy would require 500 million marks in war expenses within the first month of a future war. Afterwards, with each repetition, the amount increased. When estimating in 1906, the importance of wartime industrial mobilization was realized, and an emergency fund for this item was added, amounting to 1.4 billion marks. By 1912, the General Staff of Finance was established. The calculation of war expenses became even more serious and precise. According to the results of the department's calculations at that time, at least 2.25 billion marks of war expenses would be required in the first month of total mobilization. At the same time, the industrial mobilization expenses were set at 1.5 billion marks, and the economic emergency expenses were set at 750 million marks. The total of the three was 4.5 billion marks. This estimate was not far from the actual facts that followed. For example, from June 30 to August 1, 1914, before the war had even broken out, the average monthly mobilization expenses alone reached 1.675 billion marks. After the war broke out, the monthly war expenses required in the first year reached more than 2 billion. Thereafter, the expenses increased sharply year by year, and in the final year, the monthly war expenses required reached a maximum of 4.258 billion marks. If we compare the budgets of each period with the actual expenditures afterwards, we can also observe the trend of increase and the degree of difference.

Estimated amount of war expenses required in the first month of the war.

(Note 1) Reichs Archiv Kriegsnustung And Krieg

(Note 2) E. R. A. Seligman, Essays in taxation

From this table, we can draw the following conclusions:

First: The calculation of war expenses also changes with the change of the calculation period, increasing in a geometric progression.

Second: Although the expenses at the beginning of the war are lower than those in later periods, they need to be disbursed in large quantities immediately within a short period of time. Therefore, it is called emergency expenditure. According to the coping methods of various countries in the European War, most of these expenses rely on bank loans.

Third: After the war begins, the required amount of war expenses increases gradually. The trend also increases in a geometric progression.

Fourth: When the war is about to end, the expenditure of war expenses will inevitably create a peak. For example, the European War ended in November 1918. At that time, the war expenses of the United States averaged more than 62 million US dollars per day, exceeding all previous records. This phenomenon is probably the performance of the final struggle.

"Five" The Development and Calculation of Per-Soldier Daily Expenses During Wartime

If we use the third method to calculate the amount of war expenses required per soldier in a future war, then the difference between now and then will certainly be very large.

Before the European War, someone estimated that the war expenses required per soldier per day were 2.5 US dollars (Note 3). Someone also estimated that the war expenses required per German soldier per day were 6 marks (Note 4). This was the perspective of the early 20th century. However, after the outbreak of the European War, this estimate became problematic. Because at the beginning of the European War, the daily war expenses consumed by various countries, such as the United Kingdom, reached 9.5 million US dollars; Germany was similar to the United Kingdom; although France was lower, it also needed 8.5 million US dollars. At the peak of the war, the daily expenses were truly astonishing. For example, the United Kingdom had increased to 33.25 million US dollars, and France had increased to 11.1 million US dollars. Germany even exceeded the United Kingdom's expenses, reaching 34.25 million US dollars. As for the United States, the number was even larger: in the first two months of participation in the war, the daily demand was 15 million US dollars. A year later, it increased to 50 million US dollars. At the end of 1918, it reached 64.25 million US dollars (Note 5).

According to the daily war expenses spent by various countries in various periods, and then averaged; and then divided by the number of people mobilized in each country, we can obtain the standard amount of war expenses required per soldier per day in each country. Now we use various statistical materials and calculate using the above method, and the results are as follows:

(Note) The table is based on Seligman, Essays in taxation, Chapter 24, unit: thousands of US dollars. Based on the "Summary of War Expenses and Financial Resources of the European War" compiled by the Temporary Investigation Bureau of the Japanese Ministry of Finance, unit: thousands of Japanese yen. Based on E. Comerfurd statistics, see Zhang Yifan's "History of Disarmament Diplomacy and Warfare of the Great Powers," Chapter 2, World Book Company Publication, unit: 10,000 people.

(Note 3) Bogart, war costs and their

(Note 4) Ibid.

(Note 5) eligmap, op. cit.

According to Han's figures, the largest daily expense per soldier during the war was in the United States, estimated at 9.3 US dollars. The lowest was Austria, only 1.2 US dollars. The average is 2 US dollars per person per day, which is one-fifth higher than the pre-war estimate.

According to Japanese figures, the largest daily expense per soldier during the war was also in the United States, estimated at 15.8 Japanese yen. The smallest was Italy, only 2.6 yen. The average is 5.7 yen per person per day. However, according to Japanese scholar Hiroshi Shimozai, the average daily expense per soldier on the battlefield was 15.7 Japanese yen (Note 6), which is not much different from that estimated by Han's figures.

"Six" Future Prospects

Although the calculated numbers are absolutely inconsistent, their results all show a uniformly increasing trend. With today's high degree of military equipment and the dramatic increase in the consumption power of weapons, the scale of future wars will inevitably be larger than the European War. The war expenses required in the future will inevitably be higher than the European War. According to our following calculations, the increase rate of war expenses will reach more than nine times.

First: We first compare the recent military budgets of various countries with the military budgets of the European War, excluding the impact of price levels. The result is how much have peacetime military expenses increased? The answer is unfolded in the table above.

(Note) The pre-war military expenditure materials are based on the investigation reports of the League of Nations. All are final figures.

Today's village materials are all based on the announcements of the financial departments of various countries. The United Kingdom and Japan are the 1936 budgets. See "Where is the World Going" in Japanese, 1936 edition.

The unit is uniformly calculated in thousands of the local currency of each country.

The price index materials are based on the investigation by the Ganben Allied News Agency, see the same book.

From this comparison, we obtain several important arguments.

Today's military expenses of various countries have all increased sharply compared to before the European War. Japan and France have increased tenfold. Italy has increased fivefold. The United States has increased fourfold. The United Kingdom has increased about twofold. On average, all have increased three and one-fifth times.

Today's prices in various countries have risen only in Italy, Japan, and the United States, and have fallen in other countries. In principle, if the price level and the budget increase rate are equal, the qualitative military expenditure has not increased. If prices fall and electricity bills rise instead, then the actual increase in military expenditure is more than this number.

Italy's prices have increased threefold compared to before. Although military expenditure has increased fivefold, it has actually only increased twofold.

Japan's prices have only increased by one and a half times compared to before; military expenditure has increased tenfold. Therefore, after deducting the impact of prices, the actual increase is at least eight and one-sixth times.

The United States' prices have only increased by one and four-fifths times compared to before, but military expenditure has increased fourfold, so the actual increase is two and one-fifth times.

The prices of France and the United Kingdom have both fallen, but their military expenditure has increased. France's prices have fallen by three-tenths, but military expenditure has increased tenfold. Then the increase rate of its actual military expenditure is more than tenfold.

The United Kingdom's prices have fallen by five and eight percent; therefore, the actual increase in its military expenditure is more than twofold.

(Note 6) Investigation by First-Class Accountant Mori Takeo of Japan.

If we deduct the impact of prices from the increase in military expenditure in various countries, then the average of the pure increase is nine times. Peacetime military expenditure has purely increased fourfold, and the expense will naturally increase considerably when switching from peacetime to wartime. We might as well use a smaller-scale war as an example.

In the Russo-Japanese War in the early 20th century, according to the investigation by First-Class Accountant Mori Takeo of Japan: at that time, the daily expense per soldier per day was only 8 angles in peacetime, but 2.4 yen in wartime (Note 7). This means that wartime expenses were three times higher than peacetime expenses. Adding this peacetime increase multiple to the wartime increase multiple, the result is seven times. Then the war expenses of future wars will be seven times greater than those of the European War.

In addition, the strengthening of military equipment and the expansion of the consumption power of weapons are also the main factors that increase war expenses. Taking the total number of peacetime armies of the five major powers of the United Kingdom, the United States, Japan, France, and Italy as an example, it has increased from 1,918,000 in 1914 to 2,144,000 in 1932. The total power of naval warships has also increased from 28.17 million horsepower to 40.34 million horsepower. Roughly all have increased by one time (Note 8). As for the strengthening of the consumption power of weapons, the situation is very dramatic. Within the above-mentioned time period, the machine gun firing power of the French infantry division increased from 7,200 rounds per minute to 7,980 rounds per minute. The firing power of rifles also increased from 5,600 rounds per minute to 9,500 rounds per minute. The firing power of an artillery division also increased from 3.9 tons per minute to 14.5 tons. In the past, large aircraft could carry a maximum of 600 tons of explosives; now it has increased to 8,000 tons (Note 9). The more advanced this technology is, the greater its consumption power will be; at the same time, its own lifespan will be shorter. This not only infinitely increases the basic expenses but also increases its pure consumption. In this way, even if we combine the increase in this expense as being two times greater than that of the European War, then together with the former, it becomes nine times. In other words, that is, future war expenses will be nine times greater than the last time. If we deduct the increase rate of peacetime military expenditure and seek the increase rate of pure war expenditure, then it will also be five times.

"Seven" Trial Calculation of Our Own Situation

If this calculation is correct, then we can further try to calculate our own situation. If China is once involved in war, how much war expenses will it generally need? And most importantly, how much emergency expenses need to be prepared? Let us seek a simple answer from the following procedure:

According to the new salary quota standard of the Chinese army (Note 10), the average monthly salary of a soldier is slightly less than 14 yuan. Then each person only needs 4 jiao and 7 fen per day in peacetime (consumption of food, clothing, and weapons are all excluded). According to the experience of Japanese soldiers in the Russo-Japanese War, the expense needs to be increased threefold when changing from peacetime to wartime. Then the total war expenses required per person per day is 1 yuan, 4 jiao, and 1 fen.

According to the figures reported by the Chinese government to the League of Nations, the number of active soldiers in China in the 20th year of the Republic of China was 1,624,282 (officers are excluded). Assuming that the calculation does not increase during wartime, then at 1 yuan, 4 jiao, and 1 fen, the daily war expenses total 1,290,238 yuan. The first month would require 68,707,140 yuan. However, according to the statistics of the number of divisions and independent brigade regiments listed in the 23rd edition of the Shen Bao Yearbook, the number of active soldiers in China is at least 2,251,339. As Mu Qing statistically analyzed in his article "War and Economy," the number of troops mobilized by Russia, Germany, France, and the United Kingdom during the European War totaled 12,640,000, while there were only 2,860,000 before the war, then the number of mobilized people during wartime will increase by 4.42 times compared to peacetime. According to this situation, if the number of active soldiers in China is doubled, there will be 9,950,891 people during wartime, then the daily war expenses required will be 14,030,791 yuan, and the first month will require 420,923,720 yuan. One month's expenditure, and only what is consumed by the soldiers, will be equivalent to one-half of the total budget of the country in the 23rd year of the Republic of China. If officers are added, and equipped with the latest weapons, and an attempt is made to wage a modern war, then the war expenses, even if the total annual revenue is used to meet one day's war, is obviously not an easy task.

According to the experience of various countries, within one month after the mobilization order is issued, the required military mobilization expenses, combat mobilization expenses, naval preparedness expenses, military supplies mobilization expenses, air force preparedness expenses, and emergency expenses of various departments, etc., should at least be equal to the total amount of war expenses for one month at the beginning of the war; this must be paid immediately at the same time as the mobilization order is issued. Therefore, it is necessary to make preparations in advance. Then, in our current state of financial deficit, what method can be used to prepare? This is a question that everyone should carefully consider and catch up with urgently.

(Note 7) Mori Takeo: "Wartime Economic Control Theory," Chapter 10, Section 4

(Note 8) Zhang Yifan: "History of Military Discipline, Diplomacy, and Warfare of the Great Powers," Chapter 9, World Book Company Edition.

(Note 9) Hashimoto Kōki translated "War and Military Affairs in Russia," Part 2

(Note 10) Jia Shuyi: "Continued Financial History of the Republic of China," Part 3, Chapter 3 (End)

The Textile Industry's Self-Salvation 191

— Zhang Mengzhao

The warning signal of an extraordinary period, from the rampant smuggling in North China and the conspiracy of the strong neighbor in the background, feels that the entire national finance is being destroyed, engulfing the fertile North China plains, and holding the economic development rights. Especially the annexation plan of the textile industry and cotton-producing area in North China is most alarming. If the people's livelihood and clothing needs are to be controlled by it, the arrival of the so-called extraordinary period is imminent!

Abyssinia's demise! It was destroyed under the hard military invasion. Today, the strong neighbor treats us with military invasion as the warp and economic invasion as the weft, implementing a unified foreign policy toward China, which is a consistent continental advancement policy. The presence of military personnel in the various economic invasion organizations that steal the economic rights of North China, the commercialization of the military, and the militarization of commerce, all working together, are all carefully planned and aim to seize the real power of politics and economy. Our country's textile industry, which is in danger, has encountered an extraordinary attack.

The Current Situation of Chinese Textile Factories

Everyone knows the difficult environment of our country's textile factories. According to Yan Xiangjun of the Yujin, Lu, and Shanxi four-province textile management association, "According to statistics, there are now 4,500,000 spindles in yarn factories in our country, with foreign yarn factories accounting for 1,500,000 spindles and Chinese businesses 3,000,000 spindles, but in recent years, due to the dumping of foreign merchants and the sluggish sales of Chinese yarn, 1,500,000 spindles have been shut down. The remaining 2 million spindles are also struggling to maintain the status quo. If we do not seek relief measures, I am afraid that we will all go bankrupt, and the sales of foreign yarn are all over the country," and so on. … However, the four major textile factories of Baocheng Temple in Tianjin, which have history and status, have fallen into the hands of foreign merchants due to excessive debts.

The Economic Relationship Between Textile Factories and the Financial Industry

Since the January 28th Incident, Chinese textile factories have been declining year by year, mainly due to the fierce dumping of foreign yarn, and sales areas, except for Guangdong and Yunnan, have almost been squeezed out. Moreover, due to frequent domestic droughts and floods, the purchasing power of rural areas has decreased sharply, and inventories have accumulated. They also suffer from high-interest debts. The closure of spindles and the suspension of work are heard of every day. Therefore, the fixed assets of real estate, machinery, and the circulating assets of flowers, yarn, cloth, etc. … are mostly mortgaged to the banking industry. Judging from the industrial loans recorded in the 24th Annual Business Report of the Bank of China, which increased by 10.88% compared to the 23rd year, it is historically considerable when combined with the city's finances. Textile factories in the industry occupy a very important position in the financial industry's investment portfolio, so the economic relationship between textile factories and the financial industry is even closer.

Textile Factory Measures During Extraordinary Periods

Our textile factories are almost concentrated on the coast, and are the first to be threatened by war. When the time comes, the enemy will use a huge army to blockade our ports, such as Shanghai, Qingdao, Tianjin…, cutting off our international business communication lines. It is inevitable that iron will run rampant in the sky, destroying the economic lifelines of industry, commerce, and finance, which are necessary for our clothing needs. Then, how to maintain the factory's life material so that it is not lacking; how to train workers and prepare wages to the full, these many pending conditions, if you are in the rain of bullets and shells, and then plan, you can't do anything. Regarding this point, the two textile experts in our country, Mr. Zhu Xianfang and Zhu Gongyang, have each made written claims, which can be borrowed from, and are also what the author wants to say.

Mr. Fang's claim:

"The textile factories in the treaty ports must transport raw cotton from the mainland, and their prices are higher than the value of local purchases in the cotton-producing area due to transportation costs. The finished products must be sold in the mainland, and the actual selling price in the yarn-selling area is lower: that is, the difference in value between the flower and yarn trade is already very detailed compared to setting up factories in the cotton-producing and yarn-selling areas. What's more, foreign textile factories use new machines, new equipment, and management personnel are extremely reasonable, and they are backed by strong funds to compete with them. How can they not be destroyed and are in danger! If you want to avoid its edge, you must concentrate the excess spindles in the city, choose the cotton-producing and yarn-selling areas, and urgently plan to move. However, this cannot be done without huge funds. It is necessary for the state bank to provide low-interest loans to help it implement it, so that it can survive and then prosper on its own. See (Textile World, Volume 1, Issue 1, My Opinion on the Regeneration of Chinese Textile Factories)

Mr. Gongquan's second floor:

"If a craftsman wants to do his job well, he must first sharpen his tools. In this fiercely competitive situation, it is impossible to compare costs and products with old and outdated machines. Our Chinese factories are short of capital and most of their machinery can be improved at any time. We can start by improving the spinning machine. Because the spinning machine in the spinning factory has the greatest relationship with the output, the product, and the most modern progress, the parts that should be improved are nothing more than the bell and the traction roller tube. For every 10,000 spindles, give 50,000 yuan in government bonds, which is enough to cope with. If a factory's spinning machine has already been improved, then the cost will be changed to other machines. As for the detailed plan for improvement, it should be jointly discussed by the government's technical personnel. The method of repaying the principal and interest of the government bonds can be repaid in installments. And the government and the financial community should quickly form a cotton trust company and restore the closed factories to operation in order to strengthen the fighting power of the national textile industry! If debts are involved, it cannot hinder government orders, endanger the great plan for national production. Even if funds are insufficient, for the sake of protecting the original national industry, it is also appropriate to issue huge government bonds, but there must be a reasonable organization and strict supervision, which will be of great help to the entire national economy."… See (ibid., The Crisis of the Chinese Textile Industry and Its Self-Salvation)

Whether it is a national bank, offering loans, or the government issuing government bonds, the urgent need for economic assistance is the same. The author believes that the national industry in extraordinary times is very important. Once a war breaks out, the import of cotton yarn and cloth will stop. The production volume in Chinese factories, not to mention self-sufficiency, is really far from the needs of the public. If the original spindles cannot be planned properly as soon as possible, it is also conceivable that all of them will be in a state of shutdown at that time. This is really a matter of great concern. The only way to deal with it now is

(A) The government immediately issues extraordinary period textile public loans of 50,000,000 yuan, which will be transferred and lent by various textile banks, and the factories will be quickly relocated inland, the machinery will be improved, and production will be increased.

(B) The government strictly prohibits the export of gold and silver, and strictly prohibits hoarding. It takes resolute measures to block foreign exchange and transfer part of the funds to textile factories to maintain factory operations and the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of workers, and to prevent the people's clothing needs from suddenly causing panic.

In addition, the implementation of employee-shareholderization, military-style training, and family-style treatment will be further explained as follows:

One, the factory side of the worker's shareholderization continues to give bonuses to excellent workers, accumulate savings on their behalf, and when there is a small amount, give them stocks and advance to the shareholder position.

"Military-style training" The working class is ignorant and has weak concepts! Train them, instill morality, discipline them, and familiarize them with their skills. Absolutely obey the orders of the industrial and vocational positions to make the work tense! Military-style general mobilization.

"Family-style treatment" The factory and the workers have a close connection. Therefore, for birth, meals, death, and burial, we should consider the welfare of the workers, such as running nursing homes, nurseries, worker savings, labor insurance, and building public cemeteries, etc.… like family flesh and blood, so that the workers can wholeheartedly be loyal to the factory.

Droplets 197

— (Xiao Bai)

Without hope, there is no effort; without setbacks, there is no progress. Therefore, failure is the mother of success, a step towards a higher level.

Extraordinary events require us to handle them with a "calm" attitude. Never constantly seek "sacrifice," which can lead to the wrong path of individual heroism.

The work of rescuing the entire national crisis requires a long-term struggle. It cannot be accomplished overnight. Therefore, today's efforts cannot be considered the end of the task, but require continued struggle tomorrow. If you only seek the pleasure of today's reckless actions and forget about tomorrow, you will be letting down the nation, the country, and yourself.

We must be fully prepared, determined to make the ultimate sacrifice, avoid empty talk, and be practical. We must use actions to prove we are not lying. We must strive forward, not backward.

A Record of the Phoenix Carriage Model 198

— Bo Ju

Our country's cultural relics have long been admired by people of various countries. It is a pity that there is no large-scale museum for study and observation. Moreover, many private collections are unwilling to be displayed publicly, so the cultural relics of past dynasties are obscured. The current Chinese Cultural Relics Exhibition Society has collected more than 2,000 precious items, and since the exhibition was held on Jing'an Temple Road in Shanghai West, it has won a lot of praise. Among them, the incident of Feng Yu Tang Yang is particularly interesting, so I will study and record it.

Tang Yang is a model. The displayed Phoenix Carriage Model is about six or seven inches high and seven or eight inches wide. The precision of the manufacturing and the integrity of the proportions are similar to what I have seen in the past, although it feels concrete and subtle, there is no difference. When I saw it today, I felt the solemnity of the emperor's clothes, which still lingered in my mind.

When Empress Dowager Cixi was buried in the mausoleum, the royal procession was a grand spectacle of human life, glory and death. A reporter from the Times witnessed the grand occasion and compared it to Wu Zetian of the Tang Dynasty. (See the Beijing Telegraph on November 27, 1909). The newspaper also said that when Cixi's golden coffin was buried in the Eastern Mausoleum, it was initially carried by eighty-four people, and later increased to one hundred and twenty people. The ceremonial guards included three yellow carriages embroidered with dragons and phoenixes, all of which had to be burned in front of the mausoleum; the funeral expenses totaled more than 1.25 million taels. When the soul tablet was returned, a grand ceremony was held for the soul tablet to enter the temple. Everything was extremely grand. The yellow carriage used by the soul tablet was dazzling, and the road it passed was called the sacred road. As it approached the capital, the Prince Regent, leading the princes and ministers, knelt to welcome it at the suburbs, passed through Zhengyangmen, entered Daqingmen, and finally arrived at the Imperial Ancestral Temple, respectfully placed among the nine emperors and thirty-five empresses.

The yellow carriage used for the above-mentioned return was pre-made by the Ministry of Internal Affairs according to the regulations, presented to the Emperor for review. The carriage was six feet six inches square and seven feet eight inches high. The entire carriage was made of gold-embroidered yellow satin, and the top was made of gold leaves, with a total of ninety-nine phoenixes, and the soul tablet was a white phoenix. The bar was also gold-lacquered with clouds, which was extremely magnificent. This carriage was no different from the one used by Cixi during her lifetime. Around the carriage's base, in addition to incense and flowers, tea, fruit, and snacks were placed. Only the golden furnace in front of the base was specially set up for the return journey and was not available at ordinary times. The carriers were guards and servants of the Imperial Guard who were well-trained, so the carriage was stable and comfortable, more so than a "Rolls Royce," but not as fast. Bland and Backhouse's "China Under the Empress Dowager," said that Cixi often dozed off in the carriage during long journeys, which shows that riding in the carriage was comfortable. I am afraid that Victoria (Gu Hongming's name for Cixi) did not have this enjoyment at the time. Cixi lived an extremely extravagant life and died with great glory. The phoenix carriage was just one thing. Putting it out can also supplement the missing parts of "The Fragrant Mist of the Imperial Carriage."

Quiet Observation 199

—

Detective Films: Then and Now 200

— Jing Guan

Since the advent of movies in China, there have been detective films, but due to environmental factors, they have never escaped the fetters of case novels. They often contain elements of martial arts and supernatural beings, or like stage plays, focus on scenery and mechanisms, which are of course naive designs.

Someone once asked Cheng Xiaoqing, a detective novelist, why his detective Huo Sang was called the Chinese Sherlock Holmes. He said that if the detective was written as wearing a hat at a rakish angle, a black gown, a protruding belly, stained fingers, and like a street gangster, the spirit and form would be diminished. Moreover, detective work is based on science, and it should be performed in a brand new posture to be exciting.

What is written in the novel is the same as what is reflected on the screen, because the nature of film is more intense than that of novels.

Mingxing Film Company produced a film called "Fei Ling Ma" last year, which was the originator of Chinese sound detective films. Whether in allegory or in the strict and righteous enlightenment of drug rejection, it has achieved considerable success in art. This time, director Xu Xinfu continued his efforts and produced a film called "The Diamond King," which targets the smuggling problem, which is now of extremely important status. There is a criticism, so the consciousness is no less important than Emerald Horse, and there are two points that are commendable in his second creation: one is the proper use of small movements; the other is the prevention of old patterns. Regarding the former, we feel that in extremely tense situations, there are often extremely flexible insertions. It is not like imported detective films, which specialize in horror and bizarre events, causing extreme anxiety and stimulation to the audience. Regarding the latter, there are no chaotic chasing scenes, no unreasonable underground secret rooms, and no excessive failures that cause people to feel disgusted. Therefore, after watching The Diamond King, we firmly believe that Chinese detective films have a bright future.

Words of Bitter and Sweet 201

— Zheng Qianxi

The tenth day of the month was the fortieth birthday of my friend Mr. Fang Shoushan. He specially set up a peach table and invited relatives and friends, which was quite creative, so I will record it. A few days ago, I received a short letter from Mr. Fang, which roughly said: "I have been bedridden for many years and thought I would not get up. Although I have lungs and stomach, there is no way to complain. I did not expect the suffering of pulmonary tuberculosis. I have consulted and taken Chinese and Western medicines almost all over the country. I have tried my best to recuperate and make a living. However, the disease has not only not helped, but has become more serious. Therefore, I know that medicine can no longer help. So I plan to dress up my wife and make preparations for death. However, on the way, I met a white-haired old man who saw me haggard and asked about my suffering. He also told me that the Shanghai Yisheng Pharmaceutical Company sold Yijincao, which is very effective in treating lung diseases. In various countries in Southeast Asia, I have often seen people with lung diseases recover after taking this herb. Why don't you try it? Why do you give up the near and seek the far? I was moved by what he said. After returning to my hometown, I found that the company was in Rendeli, Xilin Road, Zhaozhou Road, South Shanghai, and I immediately bought it and took it. In less than a month, my chronic illness disappeared. After recuperating for a hundred days, my health fully recovered. This shows that seeking medicine requires fate, and getting help requires predestination. Is there no certainty in suffering and happiness? I can only say that you are so beautiful and separated by a great sea, I can only look westward and be sad. Now that I am forty years old, I have prepared some food and wine to talk with you, and to ask for words of bitter and sweet to record my rebirth." This is also a self-congratulatory birthday. On this day, the guests all had something to offer. Poems, books, couplets and plaques were full of splendor, but limited by space, I could not record them all. But I recorded the words of bitter and sweet that Yuan Jiamei, a thirteen-year-old prodigy, answered at the banquet: "Medicine has wiped away all the sorrows, scholars come to the hall to offer praises, from the time that you have suffered, Yijincao called for your happiness."

A Record of the Leng Yue Painting Exhibition 202

— Xu Bibo

Last Sunday, I went to visit my relatives with my family and Su Shengqing, and stayed at home for a few days. Just in time, my friend Tao Lengyue was exhibiting his famous paintings in the Park Library. I went to see it. There were more than a hundred points of large and small paintings. It was a feast for the eyes. Brother Tao was busy greeting and responding to people. When my wife and I arrived, he greeted us even more warmly. In addition to talking about his philosophy, he also pointed to the righteous hall straw and pamphlets to me, saying: "The red sign on it is the Zhou's order on behalf of the two staff members of the Ministry of Railways, Xia and Zhang; because most of the paintings were ordered when they were exhibited in the capital last time; this time, Mr. Zhang saw in the Su newspaper that he was going to open a daytime exhibition, so he specially asked his friends in Su to pre-order them." From this, it can be seen that his paintings are really appreciated by people; because when I was reading that day, the visitors were simply shoulder to shoulder.

On the northeast wall, there were four colored plum blossoms hanging. One of them was titled "Han Family Spring," and the poem said: "South of the Yangtze River and north of the Yangtze River are half sand and dust, and it is suspected that Zhaoyang is in trouble. How can I listen to the Qiang flute with sadness? Leaving the customs is not the spring of the Han family." The meaning is far-reaching, and the feeling of wheat and millet grows on paper. But now, please take a closer look at the painter Tao. The Great Wall, which is regarded as an important pass and a great project, is being torn down by friendly friends, who are unloading their tents there. Sigh!
