Changing Nesting Luan Phoenix 203

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: The Fine Rain and Slanting Wind Still Leave Traces; The Night Orchid is Not Quiet, and He Writes a Letter of Severance Alone.

When he went to school the next morning, he still walked the same way, and no longer walked the alley where he had picked apricot blossoms some time ago. He went there like this in the morning. When he returned home in the afternoon, he still came back as before, and he no longer had any fantasies disturbing his heart. When he got home, he felt much more settled, took a book in his hand, and could sit down and read it slowly. After two or three days like this, Guoqi suddenly had a thought in his heart. He hadn't seen that young woman for a long time. He didn't know if she was worried, angry, or even more suspicious. It would be good to meet her again, even if it was just this once, it wouldn't matter. If she was not disappointed in herself, but she abandoned her, it would show that she was too ungrateful. Although it was not necessary to chase after her, it was not necessary to say a word to abandon her and leave her. So, after a change of mind, one afternoon, he followed the route he used to wait for people, and at a certain hour, he walked towards that alley again. Sure enough, he met Jiang Menglan just at the entrance of the narrow alley. This encounter was different from usual. After seeing him, he suddenly stopped and his face turned red. But he didn't lower his head as before. Instead, he stared at Guoqi with his eyes fixed. Although Guoqi had planned to look for Menglan, after seeing Menglan, he didn't know why, but his heart seemed to be pricked with an stimulant, and he immediately stopped his body. At the same time, he broke out in a sweat all over his body, and he felt a burst of heat coming from his spine, suddenly jumping from spring to summer. Miss Jiang probably also had a sudden feeling, so she felt her face stunned. Although she didn't smile or get angry, she looked at Guoqi quickly up and down, and then took out the handkerchief tucked in her collar, held it in her mouth, and coughed lightly twice. It seemed that she had an unspeakable nostalgia for this alley, so she leaned slightly against the foot of the wall, lowered her pink neck, and walked slowly. Guoqi lowered his head slightly, turned his body, and walked slowly as well. But in the blink of an eye, in the embarrassment, he missed the opportunity to smile and greet her again. When Guoqi got home, he felt that he had done something wrong again today. How could he not show any respect after not seeing her for several days? Besides, her attitude was also very gentle and lovely. For this kind of woman, even if she couldn't be respected like the moon god Narcissus, she shouldn't be avoided like a snake or scorpion. This time, she must suspect that I deliberately ignored her and treated her as a snake or scorpion, then my sincere heart for her would be completely wasted. Then he had a thought that forced him to continue to go back and forth in the alley with apricot blossoms from this day on. The first time he saw her, he was very calm and walked naturally. (37)

Gorky Passes Away 222

— Xiang

Maxim Gorky, the literary giant with the world's largest readership, not only in the Soviet Union but also globally, passed away in the Soviet Union on the 18th of this month. This is a major event for the world. Readers around the world will no longer be able to see more magnificent creations from this comet of human liberation.

Gorky was introduced to China many years ago and immediately gained a wide readership. Every minute of his pulse and every breath he took resonated with the vast readership in our country. This was not only true in China, but also in other parts of the world. His entire physical and spiritual being had been dissolved in the blood of the oppressed masses worldwide. He became the sole comforter and encourager of hundreds of millions of oppressed people because he had become each reader himself.

Gorky is now a great writer revered by the vast readership of the world, but the beginning of his life was extremely tragic and also extraordinarily rich. It was this tragic and rich life that made him great today. Throughout his life, he attended formal school for less than a year. After that, he spent his precious youth in a long period of wandering. He worked as a railway worker, shoemaker, baker, and so on. In this long and complex wandering life, he deeply observed the concrete forms of all levels of society, which became the source of many of his later great works. His success in self-learning and building his authority in the world of literature from a very tragic life is almost a miracle in the modern world! Those of us who are currently mired in a life that is as tragic as his, should, when we mourn him at this moment, accept with the greatest enthusiasm the greatest and most precious lessons he left us!

On the eve of the Great Revolution, the Russian Empire, in a turbulent society and an atmosphere of leaping revolutionary flames, created a great signaller of human liberation, shining on the past of Russia and the present Soviet Union, emitting a compelling light to the whole world. What kind of weather are we facing now? We need a great roarer to appear in China now!

The Fallen 223

— Dai Li

It was a late autumn evening, and Wagnernev was walking alone on the quiet Avenue Joffre. He had his hands in the pockets of his grey overcoat, his head buried low, listening to the rustle of his footsteps as he paced along.

October in South China is not as cold as early autumn in St. Petersburg; it is such a beautiful and comfortable season! However, it seemed as if the climate had changed; he felt that even the severe winter in St. Petersburg was not as cold as it was now. A gust of autumn wind blew, as if thousands of flutes were playing from the tops of the thinning trees, from the end of the street. He couldn't help but shiver and reached out to pull his collar higher. As he stroked the already frayed overcoat, his heart suddenly sank, "If it's this cold in this season, what will it be like in winter? All the clothes will have to be put on in the morning before going out, won't they?" This thought stirred up another question that constantly lingered in his mind—

"Fifteen years, fifteen years! What about life? What about life?" He was confused, as if he would never get an answer. At first, he even thought, "When will I be able to return to St. Petersburg? When will I be able to attend that magnificent dance party in the Winter Palace?" But now, this thought had somehow broken away from him; he seemed to have been deprived even of the courage to think about it.

"Damn it, you bastard, Bolshevik"! He couldn't help but mutter under his breath and spat hard.

The road seemed endless, and his footsteps rustled incessantly. The neon lights on the decorated windows of the wine shops on Avenue Joffre were like the alluring eyes of a woman, reminding him of the rich aroma of Warga wine. He seemed to smell the wine and couldn't help but swallow a few times.

The gentleman continued to walk calmly, seemingly not hearing the plea. Experience had taught Wagnernevski that asking for a few cents, or if he was lucky, a torn banknote, required walking a few more steps.

He did not begrudge the worthless words and footsteps and followed closely.

"Sir, Madam, please give me a few cents, God bless you, sir..."

With a clang, a handful of coins poured from the gentleman's hand.

At that moment, the eyes of the urchins squatting by the sidewalk immediately lit up. They crowded together and ran over, reaching for the coins on the ground.

Wagnernevski's face flushed, the veins on his forehead bulging. He raised his fists and chased the children, but as soon as he chased one away, another would run back. After all, there were many children. They picked up all the coins and stood on the opposite sidewalk, laughing.

Wagnernevski trembled with rage, his eyes moist. He lunged forward furiously, as if mad. They chased each other, cursing.

"Ha, look at this Russian bum!"

Seeing the children gradually walking away and disappearing into the darkness in the distance, Wagnernevski came to his senses and clenched his fists, cursing in broken Shanghai:

"You pig! Fuck your mother's ×!"

Another gust of autumn wind blew, as if he had had a nightmare. Two lonely tears glistened in the faint light.

The street was very quiet. From time to time, a tram rumbled past. The bright streetlights cast a long, thin shadow of him. He puffed out his chest, straightened his oil-stained tie, and walked on.

Page 18

He could clearly see the houses on both sides of the road. Silver light poured out from every open or tightly closed window. He could hear the laughter of men, women, and children inside. Perhaps they were comfortably eating dinner, with salmon and roast goose on the table. He also smelled the strong aroma of coffee... All this was like the whips in the hands of executioners, mercilessly striking him, suppressing his self-esteem, causing him to lower his head again and forget to whistle.

In the distance, a couple appeared. Perhaps they were going to the theater or taking a walk after dinner. Their steps were so synchronized. The man supported the woman, whispering softly. Wagnernevski hurriedly walked up, followed them, and said in a pleading voice:

"Sir, Madam, I haven't had lunch yet! Please..."

End of Term 224

— To Min

Wandering back from the South, I spent the winter at a friend's house, still unemployed. My friend was a clerk in a foreign firm, and his monthly income of twenty-five yuan was barely enough for his single life. Now that I, an idle boarder, had joined him, both of our lives were in a state of panic. Although our friendship didn't care about living in difficult circumstances, seeing my friend's pale face and often troubled look, I always felt uneasy. Almost every day, like a gold prospector, I patiently searched in all directions for positions that would at least provide room and board, but I returned every day with a disappointed face, only to be comforted by my friend with those contrived good words. I was really bringing harm to my friend.

So I began to pay attention to the employment section in the newspapers. From my own experience and the stories of my friends, I knew a lot about those attractive advertising phrases. But finally, I steeled myself to apply for a teaching position at a small school. Because the advertisement stated that it was a semi-voluntary position, providing room and board but only a few yuan for transportation expenses. When I read that advertisement, I felt that it was very promising for my current situation.

Following the address in the advertisement, I found the school in a small alley in Zhabei. It was a shikumen building, and from the front door, I could see the classroom with the Kuomintang flag hanging. According to local custom, the classroom was called the "living room." We poor friends knew a lot about this kind of situation. As long as the desks and blackboard were not missing, Shanghai had plenty of that kind of school. Without announcing myself, I walked straight into the courtyard. A middle-aged man wearing shorts and slippers was urinating in the corner. I don't know if my appearance suited the kind of teacher that small school wanted, but he blurted out, "Did you see the advertisement?" His disrespectful attitude was rare and made me very unhappy. I nodded slightly and casually replied that I wanted to see the principal.

"Very good! Very good!" He pulled up his pants and greeted me, "I am the principal here."

I was originally going to sit down in a grand manner, but since he was going to be my superior, I couldn't help but pretend to be polite and immediately asked his name.

"My surname is Liu, Mao Jin Dao. My given name is Guang, Guang Da Zhi Guang." He suddenly seemed to remember something and shouted a name behind him that I couldn't hear clearly. While doing so, he took out two crumpled cigarettes from his short shirt pocket, handed me one, lit it, and continued, "My school has been open for seven years, and we have many students. There are three more classrooms upstairs. An old teacher has left for a better job, and the manager he recommended was too strict, and the students' families often came to the school to make a fuss. They don't want to send their children to our school anymore..."

He recounted this story very smoothly, like a storyteller, but he suddenly stopped there. Just then, a school servant-like person brought out tea. He personally took the teacup and handed it to me, smiling and continuing:

"Sir, you are an understanding person. Reducing a student means reducing tuition, so I placed an advertisement to hire someone like the old teacher, hehe, do you understand what I mean, sir!"

Naturally, I understood completely, and I knew a lot about it. After we had settled everything, I asked him about the transportation expenses, which were not mentioned in the advertisement.

"This..." He didn't seem to have anticipated this question. After thinking for a while, he stretched out the index finger of his right hand. "The school is really poor. Just like before, ten yuan, ten yuan."

The school started in just three days. Two people managed the stairs. The students, when they came to school, seemed to be entering a park, bringing some food and chattering noisily in the classroom. They didn't want to study at all. It was best to tell stories every hour, or rather, every day. And our Principal Liu Guang seemed to be a story expert. He could tell stories about the dull son-in-law, the Dragon King's birthday, and Xue Rengui's expedition to the east.

He, guarding against my opposition to that kind of teaching method, said to me that dealing with those students was best done haphazardly, as long as they were happy and the tuition money came in. Last year's teacher was not lenient and almost sent all the students away.

Since I had entered a story-telling school, I also became a storyteller, but I peddled stories about Washington, Napoleon, and Sun Yat-sen, because I had to be worthy of the ten yuan a month for transportation expenses.

At the end of the third month, Liu Guang discussed with me that the fee would be paid in a few days. Since I didn't have much use for it, I agreed. But the fourth and fifth months were still owed. He said that he would pay it all at the end of the term. He was thinking of a way to make sure that there would be more students next semester.

About ten days before the end of the term, he left and did not return to school. The next day, bailiffs came to move the desks. Only then did I find out that Liu Guang had not paid the rent for four months, and he had run away himself. Ending a semester of storytelling life, I lived at my friend's house again.

Third-Class Ward 225

— Lao Xin

When I heard the news that Ren was suffering from typhoid fever, I anxiously discussed it with Qi and decided that as soon as we had some free time, we would go to the ×× Hospital to see him. Who knew that day after day passed, and we couldn't find the time to go see him. At the time, we really felt guilty, especially when we mentioned such a homeless young man during idle conversations. We both sighed for him and repeatedly remembered his story. One day, Qi went out early in the morning and called back around noon! —

"Ren's illness has reached a critical stage. You must come to the hospital once. Maybe this is our last chance to see him. Zong, come on, I'm waiting for you at the hospital now!..."

Without even having time to notify my colleagues, I jumped on the bus. The rush at the time was really impossible to recall. I had rarely forgotten everything like that before. Today was probably because the news was too shocking. After arriving in front of the Ministry of Finance, I changed to the bus to Dongshan, and only then did I feel a little more settled. At this time, I remembered this young friend who had no motherland, and everything he had encountered in the past few years. I had almost become neurotic. I remembered that it was only about a week before he got sick that we were still working on something very interesting together. His firm, stubborn, and strong words still remained in our minds and would not be forgotten—never forgotten. However, it had only been a few days, and a strong man was entangled by illness, and it was the very aggressive typhoid fever. Then, his wife sent him to the hospital, notified his friends, and asked his friends to donate money. In this way, not only did our interesting matter come to an end, but our happiness was also swallowed up by this disease demon.

The car stopped abruptly. As if something was pulling us, we jumped out of the car in two steps. A very grand and elegant building lay before me. It was like a dark shadow pressing heavily on my chest, covering my eyes. My heart was still very anxious, but my footsteps became slower, just like an attendant in a funeral procession. After notifying the gatekeeper, I turned a corner at the stairs. The stairs were covered with a carpet, and there was no sound when I walked on them in leather shoes, but I was even more careful, my steps becoming slower and slower, and my chest felt heavy and suffocating.

"Zong!"

A very familiar voice startled me. Like before, I didn't make a fuss, only using soft eyes to comfort her, meaning to advise her not to be too sad. However, my eyes were too foolish and had no effect at all. On the contrary, they were like a cruel executioner, drawing out her sorrow. She said, with tears in her eyes:

"Zong, there is no hope for him. The doctor said: If his temperature continues to rise, then no one can say for sure."

Ren's firm, stubborn, and strong words were shaking in my ears like copper bells again. I cruelly bit my own lips, begging her to accompany me to the ward to see Ren.

It was a third-class ward. A dark and small room, with four beds placed horizontally and vertically, leaving only a narrow aisle to run through sideways. The air was very bad, and I couldn't stand the sickening smell of medicine. I doubted that this would be a suitable room for patients who were not in a critical condition, but I had long heard that he was lucky enough to be moved to this almost second-class ward. Otherwise, a large compartment with seven or eight people would be even more nauseating than this.

Ren was lying on the bed against the wall. He was sound asleep at this time. His face, set off by the snow-white quilt, was old and dark, flushed with heat, very haggard, and a water bag wrapped in white cloth was placed on his forehead to reduce his discomfort a little. We suffocated in this terrifying third-class ward, not wanting to wake him up, and not wanting to leave him like this.

After a while, his dry lips moved a few times, and his dry tongue licked between his lips weakly for a while. Then he muttered deliriously:

"Life! Afraid of his tortoise, everyone fight him this time! Come on, come on, as long as I..."

I was flustered and a little out of control, and went up to cover his mouth with my hand. I was afraid he would say something. Rather than break the rules of the hospital ward, we woke him up. He opened his eyes with great effort, his lifeless, deathly yellow eyes. I was afraid to look at them, I endured the onslaught of all the pain.

"Zong, is that you?"

I stared at him. He was already very tired and couldn't continue speaking. At this time, I forgot that I had once cursed others for not using lies to deceive a dying person, and I began to say things that I didn't want to say.

Finally, Qi pulled me away from this terrifying third-class ward. We went back to the road. At this time, our topic turned to complaining about the third-class ward that could only kill people and not heal them.

After a few days of rainy and muggy weather. One afternoon, Ren's wife called, reporting to us simply, as if without any sadness: Ren is dead.

Bull Nose, Planting Flowers is Difficult 226

— Huang Yao

Broadcasting, Broadcasting Script

People of Suzhou (23) 227

— Written by Gu Wenzong

Liya: Thank you for your kindness! I'm leaving! Goodbye!

Jinghong: Can we meet again?

Liya: If I don't die, there will always be a day to meet again.

Jinghong: I hope you don't die so we can see each other more often.

Liya: I will definitely not disappoint you.

Jinghong: Thank you, God!

Liya: You should thank me.

Jinghong: Then thank the Queen Mother of the West.

Liya: I don't like people complimenting me and joking like that!

Jinghong: Then I sincerely thank the Suzhou Miss Jin.

Liya: Why do you have to add the title "Suzhou Miss"?

Jinghong: Then let's eliminate the title "Suzhou Miss".

Liya: It shouldn't have been added in the first place!

Narrative Singing 229

He Yun and He Qin Fang Double Pearl Ballad

China and the West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Eyes Straining to See Distant Geese"

Beautiful maiden gazes in the mirror like a hibiscus. Parting with her beloved is heartbreaking. When you left, you promised me, when the willows are green and the peaches are red, we would meet again. Why mention, the Dragon Boat Festival, celebrating the red pomegranate. Spring goes and spring comes. Autumn arrives again. The Cowherd and Weaver Girl meet through letters. Pushing open the window to view the bright autumn moon, Chang'e tightly closes the Guanghan Palace. Autumn passes again. Winter comes early. Cold winds blow in gusts. Hating the palace. Snow falls. Lonely woman fears the remaining winter. Hating the wronged souls. Such cold weather. May they not suffer loneliness. Must meet a kindred spirit with deep affection. If they don't come in this lifetime, so be it. Sending a sealed letter to cut off all communication. So that I won't always worry.

Xu Wenbi's Opening

Tongle (720) 1:00 AM to 1:45 AM

Opening "Romance of the Western Chamber"

A scholar's favor is worth half a sheet of paper. An ounce of silver furnishes a Zen hall. Most delighted by the splendor of the Three Treasures Land. Meditating and listening to the explanation of the Vajra Sutra. The cuckoo sings lonely at my ears. A traveler's inn in a strange land is even more desolate. This place is, clear phoenix, bright moon, unattended. Resting and stopping at the Western Chamber. Sitting idly in the small pavilion, studying the principles of change. Reading books by the light of the firefly window. A pair of monks and laymen speaking noisily. A young maid walks out. To comply with Madame Cui's orders. A Buddhist service is held in the Zen room. First, the late Prime Minister's death anniversary. Please ask the monk to recommend him to the Western Paradise. On the fifteenth auspicious day, worship the Dharma King. Having finished speaking, he wants to leave but hesitates. Because of a love-stricken, powdered young man. Zhang Sheng approaches and bows deeply. Elder Sister, are you the maid Hongniang of Miss Yingying? I am, Zhang Junrui, a talented scholar from Luoyang. Using the temple as a study for the sake of marriage. Please report to the Palace of Rui Zhu. Say that I, still have no wife at home. Hongniang hears, her face changes. What you say is outrageous. It is said from ancient times that one should not speak improper words. A bookish gentleman dares to be frivolous. Old-fashioned people uphold principles of frost and snow. Three-foot children are not allowed to enter the central hall. It can be forgiven that a maid hears the words. The mistress will hate it very much if she finds out. From now on, think before you speak.

Movies

Odds and Ends 231

The Wednesday Experimental Little Theater held its second public performance at the Xinguang Grand Theater yesterday morning at 9:30 AM. The plays were "A Corner of the Metropolis", "Autumn Sun" and "Smuggling". However, when "A Corner of the Metropolis" was performed halfway, it was suddenly interrupted. The reason was that the concession authorities did not allow the play "Smuggling" to be staged, and "Autumn Sun" and "A Corner of the Metropolis" also had to be partially deleted and revised. After an hour of consultation, the theater finally demanded to finish performing "A Corner of the Metropolis", but because there was a line in the play, "The Northeast is our territory", the performance was eventually forced to stop. The audience sat quietly and waited, and the order was very good. Reality Experiment is immediately rehearsing a new play, preparing to be staged next Sunday.

Chen Juanjuan's "Lost Lamb" song has been recorded into a record by Baidai Company. Baidai recently auditioned it and specially invited Cai Chusheng, Chen Juanjuan, Ge Zuozhi, and others to listen. It is said that the results were excellent.

After the "Go to Nature" Ganpu location shooting team returned, they immediately shot outdoor scenes of the desert island wooden house for days. Both male and female actors were half-naked while acting. The location of the outdoor scenes for "Mr. Wang's Knight-Errant Biography" has been decided to be Yixing, and the special issue has also begun to be edited.

Hu Die will build a new house. The design has been decided, and it is the most popular and novel palace style, with a basketball court, tennis court, pavilions, long corridors, gardens, and clear streams. The building and the site are very tortuous and comfortable, just like a small-scale palace. It is said that the design of the house was designed by Wu Yaqing, a scenic designer from the Star Film Company.

Zhang Yi lost the pipe given by Hunan movie fans along with his wallet on the way to the factory to shoot "A Mother's Love Song" a few days ago. Just because the pipe was engraved with Zhang Yi's name, it was returned by the person who picked it up the next day.

Kunhe Tobacco Company specially made two kinds of cigars for "Mr. Wang" and "Xiao Chen". The one smoked by "Mr. Wang" is long and thin, and the one smoked by "Xiao Chen" is short and thick.

Ant Troupe Changes Repertoire 232

The Ant Troupe held its third public performance at the Lake Society (Beijing Road) on the 23rd. The plays to be performed were originally decided to be the three one-act plays "Smuggling", "Who Killed the Baby?" and "Bugle". It is said that the play "Who Killed the Baby?" was not approved because the content was slightly inappropriate for this year's "Year of Child Implementation", so it was not approved. It is now said that the troupe has decided to replace it with "Poison", but because the performance date is too close, the situation of rehearsing day and night these days is very tense.

Wan's Photo Studio Special News 233

Wan's Photo Studio, No. 510 to 512, Huaihai Road, Shanxi South Road, is organized by the Wan Brothers: Xiangming, Guchan, Chaolu, and Dixuan, Chinese cartoonists. The photography products have long been famous in Shanghai. Wan Dixuan personally operates the camera. His experience in photography, the combination of light, and the use of skills are all aimed at making the pictures beautiful and the lens angles excellent. It is the best treasure house in Shanghai for taking photos of contemporary stars and the art palace for fashionable ladies' photos. The prices for art photos and other categories are also very low. Now the work part has been expanded and the latest type of flushing and drying motors have been added, as well as many new beautiful art scenes, all designed by famous artists.

"Little Tiger" Published 234

Zhou Tianji's recent book takes the tragic life of Little Tiger as the weft and the social dark side as the warp. The plot is bizarre and twists and turns, and the writing style is lively and relaxed. Those who have read "Sweet Sweet" do not need to be told more. The entire book is a thick volume illustrated by Mr. Hua Junwu, which can be described as a perfect combination. The entire book is printed in letterpress, and each copy sells for three cents and five points. Published by Wenguang Bookstore, all bookstores are selling it.
